Current Affairs Commentary

The Hirota Cabinet's Diplomatic Policy Towards the United States 17

— Xing

Hirota Koki, as a diplomat, was ordered to form a cabinet to cope with the extraordinary situation after the February 26th Incident. General observations indicate that this is a clear sign that Japan's future national policy will not be radicalized. However, the policies expressed by Hirota in recent days are all based on the original intentions of the young military officers. In terms of diplomacy, it will adopt an active policy towards China and Russia, and towards Europe and the United States, it will take coordination as the surface and practical interests as the bone. The so-called Hirota's Three Principles for China want to make China a vassal of Japan. The so-called withdrawal of the Soviet Far East Army is tantamount to demanding that the land east of Lake Baikal be incorporated into the Japanese Empire. Furthermore, in order to seek to independently use troops against Russia without any worries, Japan intends to have the United States automatically withdraw from the Far East. According to Hirota's latest statement, what Japan requires from the United States is the redistribution of economic resources, the opening of markets and free trade, and the lifting of immigration restrictions. In addition, Japan is more willing to conclude mutually beneficial economic agreements and politically mutual security treaties with the United States.

Can Hirota develop his diplomatic aspirations? Can the United States accommodate such demands? Will Japan-US relations be improved by this, so that Japan can concentrate its efforts on dealing with China and Soviet Russia? Regarding the so-called redistribution of world resources, Japan once proposed it at the London Naval Conference. Mr. Amau, the spokesman of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, has repeatedly cited the words of Colonel House of the United States and former British Foreign Secretary Hoare as the basis for this requirement (they believed that countries that are strong but not rich can discuss with those that are both rich and strong, such as Britain and the United States, the method of sharing world resources). However, although the United States is rich in natural resources, nineteen of them are in the United States mainland. Outside the mainland, such as Alaska, Hawaii, the Philippines, and Central America, are all places coveted by Japan. Can the United States allow Japan to interfere in these areas and seize the natural resources on which American industry depends? The so-called opening of markets and free trade are aimed at the tariff barriers of the United States and the anti-Japanese policies of various countries in Central and South America. However, even under such restrictions, Japan's commercial aggression against the Americas has achieved great success. According to the report released by the Tariff Commission in Washington on the 10th of this month, Japan's exports last year have exceeded the height of 1929, which is unmatched by any country in the world, and the largest part of the increase in exports is in the Central and South American markets.

Recently, Japanese goods have not only invaded Central and South America, which have always been the forbidden territory of American business circles, but also invaded the markets of the United States mainland. This development has caused great panic in the American industry. Under the current situation, Hirota wants the United States to open up its markets for Japan to allow the free flow of Japanese goods, which may not be accepted by the United States. As for the immigration issue, since the United States abolished the Gentlemen's Agreement in 1924, the bad relationship between Japan and the United States has centered on this issue. The Japanese population increases by one million every year. If Japan requires the United States to unconditionally accept Japanese immigrants, the United States will never accept it before the country is destroyed. If Japan only requires that Japanese immigrants to the United States receive the same treatment as immigrants from other countries, then according to the current US immigration law, Japan can only immigrate one or two hundred people to the New World each year. A drop in the bucket, what can it do to solve the accident? The American people have extremely suspicious and fearful psychology regarding the freedom of immigration for Japanese people, and under this kind of psychology, it is also impossible to abolish the anti-Japanese laws in the United States.

The economic development of Japan and the United States has reached a point of mutual conflict. In the past, Japan transported raw silk to the United States and the United States swiftly traded cotton to Japan, without interfering with each other. Today, Japan's exports are mainly industrial products, such as cotton cloth, electrical materials, and rayon, which are in a situation where they cannot coexist with American export goods. In the direction of China and South America, there is fierce competition. Therefore, it is difficult to establish an economic agreement that is beneficial to both parties. Moreover, since Japan announced the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty and withdrew from the London Naval Conference, the collective peace of the Pacific has been completely destroyed. The two countries are competing to establish military equipment to plan for a war. Hirota's hope of success in his policy towards the United States is very slim, and Japan's desire to devote all its efforts to military affairs on the mainland without any worries is just a beautiful fantasy.

According to the news obtained by the diplomatic correspondent of "Le Petit Parisien", Foreign Minister Flandin will submit four proposals to the League of Nations Council this afternoon:

French Foreign Minister Submits Four Proposals to the League of Nations; The League of Nations Association Must Maintain its Prestige in this One Fell Swoop; Otherwise, It Can Only Consolidate Itself with Allied Countries 18

One of the issues that the Franco-Russian Mutual Assistance Treaty is in conflict with the Locarno Treaty is that France is willing to submit it to the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague for adjudication.

Before the Council of the League of Nations makes a decision on Germany's abolition of the treaty, it should immediately take preventive measures to prevent Germany from increasing the number of troops along the Rhine and building fortifications.

After the Council has made a decision, the mutual assistance clauses contained in the Locarno Treaty should be implemented immediately.

The British and French governments should immediately discuss appropriate measures to safeguard the security of both countries, prevent future threats from Germany, and negotiate and sign a new treaty to replace the Locarno Treaty.

The diplomatic correspondent of "Le Petit Parisien" also said that if this proposal by France is rejected, the country's enthusiasm for the League of Nations will inevitably be greatly reduced, or even return to its past alliance policy and consolidate itself with allied countries. (Havas Electric dispatch from the 16th)

League of Nations Letter Sent; Berlin Considering Reply 19

London: The Council of the League of Nations has recently decided to formally invite Germany to send representatives to England in the capacity of a signatory to the Locarno Treaty and to attend the Council meeting at 3:30 PM on the 16th to present a reply to the application submitted by France and Belgium. This invitation has been telegraphed by Ivanoe, the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, to the Berlin government. (Havas Electric dispatch from the 14th)

Berlin: The Council of the League of Nations has recently formally invited Germany to send representatives to attend the Council meeting. How Germany should reply to this matter, political figures are extremely tight-lipped. It is reported that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is quite hesitant. Foreign Minister Neurath held consultations with Director Blow of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Director of British Affairs Tieckhoff, and Hitler's confidant Ribbentrop, etc., until 8:00 PM. It is generally believed that the German reply will be sent to London tomorrow morning. According to semi-official sources, if Germany accepts the invitation and sends representatives to attend the Council meeting, then Ribbentrop and Tieckhoff will be selected to go to London. (Havas Electric dispatch from the 14th)

Locarno Signatories Quietly Awaiting League of Nations Resolution; Temporarily Delaying Further Plans 20

London: The representatives of the Locarno Treaty signatories, England, France, Belgium, and Italy, met in the British Foreign Office this afternoon to discuss and agree to temporarily refrain from taking any possible plans against Germany's action of abolishing the treaty, so as not to hinder the resolution of the Council of the League of Nations. According to the public report, once the Council of the League of Nations has decided on the document submitted by France and Belgium, the four countries will meet again. Before the meeting today, the British delegation had consulted with Prime Minister Baldwin and other cabinet members at 10 Downing Street. (Reuters Electric dispatch from the 14th)

London: The meeting of the Locarno Treaty signatories continued at 5:20 PM and ended at 6:57 PM. Those who participated in the meeting were French Foreign Minister Flandin, Minister without Portfolio Peng Gu, Belgian Prime Minister Jilin, Italian Ambassador Grandi, British Foreign Secretary Eden, Privy Councilor MacDonald, Justice Minister Hailsham, and Finance Minister Chamberlain. Prime Minister Jilin of Belgium proposed yesterday to submit the issue of whether the Locarno Treaty and the Franco-Russian Mutual Assistance Treaty conflict with each other to the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague for adjudication, and at this time, to immediately start negotiations with Germany in accordance with the proposal made by Hitler. After the meeting today, French Foreign Minister Flandin opposed the proposal made by the Belgian Prime Minister, saying that this proposal should be discussed after the Council of the League of Nations announces that Germany has violated the treaty. He also advocated that all member states of the League of Nations should assist the Locarno Treaty signatories so as to restore the Rhine region to its original state in accordance with the provisions of Article 4, Paragraph 2 of the treaty. (Note: Article 4, Paragraph 2 of the Locarno Treaty states that whenever an act that destroys this treaty or violates Articles 42 and 43 of the Treaty of Versailles occurs, the Council of the League of Nations, once it is aware of it, shall immediately notify the signatories of this treaty, and each country promises to immediately provide assistance to the country that is the object of this violation.) After the meeting, a public report was issued stating, "The meeting of the Locarno Treaty signatories continued to exchange views today and decided to convene the next meeting after the Council of the League of Nations has taken a decision on the application matters of France and Belgium." Before the meeting today, French Foreign Minister Flandin had consulted with French Prime Minister Sarraut on the long-distance telephone to discuss the current situation. Flandin was originally scheduled to return home in the middle of next week to consult with the cabinet on the situation, but after this decision was made, the trip to Paris has been cancelled. (Havas Electric dispatch from the 14th)

London: According to sources from the French delegation, France is now prepared to submit the issue of the Locarno Treaty and the Franco-Russian Mutual Assistance Treaty being in conflict with each other to the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague for adjudication. However, this issue should be submitted to the Hague Court by the Council of the League of Nations, and the governments of the countries concerned should also declare to the Council in advance that they are willing to accept the judgment of the Hague Court before it can be submitted. (Havas Electric dispatch from the 14th)

Hitler Inspires the People, Fighting for Freedom and Equality, Unwilling to Endure International Tribunal Judgments, Prefers Severing Ties with Other Countries if Goals Aren't Met 21

Munich - The German Führer Hitler delivered a speech here today, stating that Germany will refuse the invitation to the League of Nations Council meeting in London on Monday. Germany cannot long endure the judgments of international tribunals. We will ignore threats and warnings. We can no longer tolerate unequal status, as it easily leads to rebellion and international hatred and fear. How can peace be achieved if one country is driven by hatred and another is dominated by mistrust? I do not want to make gestures that would damage Germany's honor. The whole world knows that Germany in 1918 was treated in a certain way, and they all believe that they can treat Germany today as they did then, but the reality is quite different. Our principle is that if other countries treat us equally, we are willing to cooperate; otherwise, we would rather sever ties. Germany deeply desires to conclude a Franco-German pact guaranteed by Britain and Italy, stipulating that in case of disputes, the League of Nations should determine who the aggressor is. Before France and Russia concluded a mutual assistance pact, I was determined to abide by the Locarno Treaty and allow the signatory countries themselves to determine who the aggressor was. I know that the time to implement this decision is approaching. France accuses Germany of being the aggressor. The subsequent changes are obvious. Many countries still regard Germany as the instigator of the First World War. This shows how easy it is to fabricate rumors. (National News Agency, 14th)

Munich - Führer Hitler delivered an election speech in the open square here tonight. (The House of Representatives is scheduled to hold a by-election on the 29th of this month.) Forty special trains transported 300,000 people from various parts of Bavaria to listen to the speech. Hitler was originally scheduled to arrive here at 8 p.m., but due to drafting a reply to the League of Nations Council (the League of Nations Council has formally invited Germany to send representatives to attend the meeting to be held on Monday), an important meeting was held in Berlin in the afternoon, so his arrival was delayed until 9:30 p.m. The leaders of the National Socialist Party held a meeting at the "Vier Jahreszeiten Kempinski" hotel, presided over by the Führer himself, and had numerous telephone conversations with the Berlin Foreign Ministry. After the National Socialist Party meeting ended, the Führer drove to the open square, where 300,000 people cheered in unison. Amidst the rumble of celebratory cannons, Hitler ascended the podium with his head held high and spoke in impassioned words, "I ask the entire nation to support me so that I can strive and fight for the honor and rights of the country. This is the third time since 1933 that I have done so. My rearmament is not a game. On the contrary, I do not want our country to be attacked by other countries, hence this action. Peace cannot be realized if any nation does not obtain equal rights. I firmly believe this. The German nation is despised and treated worse than others. This is something I will never tolerate."

Hitler then said that after the German army entered the Rhineland, France asked Germany to make a compromise, saying, "As for the so-called compromise, I do not know what it means. What I have done is more than a compromise, because my words and deeds are consistent. I believe that the world will eventually be peaceful, but if other countries continue to oppress the oppressed nations, causing their desire for revenge to never be forgotten, how can the world order last? As for those who created the Treaty of Versailles, they were foolish and presumptuous in wielding their pens, and they had no foresight about the consequences. Now, after the signing of various treaties, many new facts have emerged before our eyes. Therefore, it is impossible to succeed without embracing a grand vision of sacrifice and modifying the current treaties based on facts. As for the continuous warfare to rectify Germany's borders, this is not what Germany desires," and so on. Before Hitler arrived at the meeting, Wagner, the leader of the National Socialist Party in this city, gave a speech to the crowd, saying, "We are here tonight because the world is full of falsehood and hypocrisy, and we must express our protest. The Führer Hitler's goal is to restore the German people to their inherent honor. We will never accept those who accuse us of tearing up treaties," and so on. After Hitler's speech tonight, the National Socialist Party's Stormtroopers held a large-scale parade, with members carrying torches and passing through the streets, with flags hanging everywhere along the way, creating a very enthusiastic atmosphere. (Havas News Agency, 14th)

Führer Hitler recently delivered an election speech here, with the final paragraph saying, "Germany is a great nation in Europe, and other countries must treat it as a great nation." The Locarno Treaty, in Germany's view, is actually a "Truce of God" between Germany, France, and Belgium. (In the mid-11th century, Catholic bishops held a meeting in Nicaea and promulgated laws prohibiting believers from engaging in violence between Wednesday and the following Sunday, which is the so-called Truce of God.) At this point, Hitler again criticized the mutual assistance pact between France and Russia, saying, "Since France, Russia, the Czech Republic, and France have respectively established this pact, they can attack Germany at any time. I am the German Führer and am responsible for the country. I must consider the country's future. Moreover, after the establishment of the mutual assistance pact between France and Russia, no one can guarantee that communism will not harm France and Germany." Finally, Hitler reiterated the various peace proposals of Sweden and said that the House of Representatives will be re-elected on the 29th of this month so that the people can express their opinions on whether the Führer's policies are good or bad, whether Germany is richer or poorer, and whether the Führer can represent the people in the world. "I hope that the people can express their faith in their Führer on this day so that I can proclaim to the world that my words and deeds are not something I have obtained privately, but rather a manifestation of the German people's will," and so on. (Havas News Agency, 14th)

Difficult for Britain to Deal with the German Question, Cabinet Opinions Not Unified, Sanctions May Be Difficult to Implement 22

London - According to parliamentary sources, if France insists that Britain fulfill its obligations under the Locarno Treaty regarding Germany's abrogation of the treaty, the result will cause a storm in the British cabinet. All cabinet members acknowledge that these obligations are indeed valid, but most cabinet members are realists who, due to the unsuitable timing and dissenting public opinion, are unwilling for Britain to fulfill all of its obligations. Foreign Secretary Eden and Lytton Goebbels do not think so. If the two are forced by circumstances to demand that the cabinet adopt a tough attitude towards Germany, and all cabinet members cannot agree, the two will resign. Prime Minister Baldwin knows that once the two resign, it will be difficult for the cabinet to obtain the support of the majority in the House of Commons, so he feels quite embarrassed. Generally, when the cabinet met this afternoon, in addition to discussing the current situation, it also studied the negotiations among the signatory countries of the Locarno Treaty and what repercussions it would have on British domestic affairs. It is rumored that six cabinet members advocate that the British cabinet take action to assist France's minimum demands (referring to restoring the Rhineland to its original state) and strive to achieve it. In that case, the number of hardliners in the cabinet has now increased. (Havas News Agency, 14th)

London - Former Secretary of the Navy Churchill gave a speech in Birmingham yesterday, stating that if the League of Nations is unable to punish powerful aggressor countries, and Britain must deal with aggression alone in the future, once this situation is confirmed, the entire principle of collective security will be destroyed, the League of Nations will be completely defeated, and Britain will suffer great pain and shame. As for Germany's abrogation of the treaty, we must make it restore the rule of law before we can start negotiations. If the League of Nations is weak and incompetent and fails, we can only restore the old alliance system and resolve all disputes by force. (Havas News Agency, 15th)

London - Regarding the issue of implementing sanctions against Germany, various military sanctions, such as sending troops to occupy the Rhineland, which could lead to war, have been rejected. The only remaining option is economic sanctions. British officials believe that Germany's deployment of troops to the Rhineland is a violation of Articles 42 and 43 of the Treaty of Versailles. Although the treaty is related to the League of Nations Covenant, Germany's actions cannot be regarded as a violation of the Covenant. Therefore, taking collective action to sanction Germany in accordance with the provisions of the Covenant is flawed and can be criticized in legal terms. The League of Nations Council passed a resolution on April 17 last year, advocating economic sanctions against countries that violate treaty obligations. This resolution can be used as a basis, but economic sanctions should be implemented only with the unanimous approval of the representatives of the Council's member states, which may be difficult to achieve. (Havas News Agency, 14th)

Germany Makes Overtures to Italy, Ambassador to Italy Delivers Speech in Rome, Comparing Bismarck and Cavour 23

Rome - German Ambassador to Italy Hassel gave a speech here yesterday on the achievements of German Prime Minister Bismarck and Italian Prime Minister Cavour, stating that international treaties can resolve disputes for a time but cannot create lasting peace. The status quo they stipulate must be overthrown. This is why major events have occurred in the Red Sea and the Rhineland. What we hope for is that the great spirit displayed by Prime Minister Mussolini four years ago when he initiated the Four-Power Pact can be seen again today, so that new treaties can be established and the situation of division and disintegration in Europe can be clarified. Bismarck and Cavour are models for Europeans, not narrow-minded nationalists. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and German Führer Hitler have completed the great cause of unification. We must serve with common virtues to realize Cavour's motto of "unity and peace." (Havas News Agency, 15th)

London - Regarding Germany's abrogation of the Locarno Treaty, well-informed sources here claim that the German government has notified Italian Prime Minister Mussolini that Italy is unlikely to support the application submitted by France and Belgium to the League of Nations Council yesterday. If it does, Germany will implement the sanctions that the League of Nations decided on against Italy due to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, as if Germany were a member of the League of Nations. (Havas News Agency, 15th)

Italy Maintains Neutrality, Italian Undersecretary Declares to German Ambassador 24

Paris - A Paris Midi reporter in Rome recently claimed that German Ambassador to Italy Hassel informed Italian Undersecretary Suvich yesterday that Germany still maintains its original attitude regarding the rearmament of the Rhineland. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini is absolutely neutral, and Suvich confirmed this intention to Hassel. (Havas News Agency, 15th)

France Strengthens Eastern Defenses, Transfers Troops to Guard Strategic Locations 25

Paris - The French Army Committee recently finished reviewing the defense works along the Rhineland and decided that the troops stationed in various towns have been transferred to strengthen border defenses, leaving them empty. Therefore, reinforcements must be sent to fill them. Troops have been heading to eastern France in a steady stream in recent days. Two infantry regiments entered Toul today to reinforce the garrison there. Other troops will be stationed at strategic locations within the defense zone from Sedan to Strasbourg. (Reuters, 15th)

Germany Increases Rhineland Garrison, Heavy Artillery Arrives in Saarlouis, Wehrmacht Surveys Terrain Day and Night 26

London - According to news received today from Metz, Germany has not only not withdrawn its troops from the Rhineland but has increased them. It is reported that successive heavy artillery detachments have been transferred to Saarlouis, and a regiment of artillery from Ulm has also been added to the garrison in Karlsruhe. The Underground Resources of China and the Strength of the Nation 63

— Weng Wenying

Weng Wenying, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, delivered a speech at a secret meeting in the capital some days ago. The text of his speech has now been compiled and is presented below.

Gentlemen, the topic I am discussing today is "China's Underground Resources and the Strength of the Nation." Confucius said, "If a craftsman wants to do his job well, he must first sharpen his tools." If the tools are not good, the work will not be good. We can apply this principle to all other matters. When someone asked Confucius what the conditions for establishing a state were, Confucius said, "Sufficient food, sufficient military, and the trust of the people." This statement encompasses three aspects: preparedness, ample resources, and faith in the country. The term "food" includes not only food grains, and "military" includes not only guns and cannons, but also all necessary materials. Broadly speaking, this begins with the metallic resources underground. In ancient times, the relationship was still small, but in modern times, it is of great importance. Modern archaeological conclusions divide human culture into three periods: the Stone Age, the Bronze Age, and the Iron Age. This kind of division existed in ancient China. For example, the Wu Yue Chunqiu and Yue Jue Shu both have similar records. At that time, the southern states of Wu and Chu were strong, and many crafts were passed down through specialized families, concentrated in the hands of a few. These families knew the history of their trade very well. Yue became strong by casting swords with iron. Chu asked the Wu person Feng Huzi about the materials used for casting weapons. Feng Huzi replied: "The military instruments have gone through three eras. Yu used jade and (muscle stone) as weapons; the Xia dynasty used bronze as weapons; and now we use iron as weapons. Only by using iron for military instruments can the nation become prosperous." However, with the advancement of modern culture, we are no longer in the age of iron, but in the age of steel. Steel weapons are stronger than iron. We not only need to use steel, but also need to produce large quantities of coal. Coal provides power, and power comes from coal and oil. Coal and oil both come from mineral deposits. There are many famous minerals today that were unknown to people in the past. For example, the element antimony. The Chinese language did not even have a corresponding character, so people did not know about it. This is also true for tungsten ore. There is a very special kind of tungsten ore in Hunan, which is slightly different from wolframite. It is called "the son of the lump of fire," something not found in dictionaries. Its discovery is more recent than that of antimony. It was discovered in southern Hunan around the years of the Republic, and it is the world's number one tungsten ore. This kind of ore has extremely important uses, especially in the manufacture of military instruments, where it is a necessary raw material. Modern countries must first have large-scale production, second must have power, and third must have important components. If a country does not have essential mineral resources, it cannot accomplish any of these three things. Now I will talk about the main mineral resources that have national and international significance, especially in China. We should view these issues with the standard of "treating others as we would like to be treated, and forgiving others as we forgive ourselves."

Steel and Iron. Steel and iron are the most important things among mineral resources. China uses 600,000 tons of steel annually, while the world produces 70 million tons annually. China uses less than one percent of the total. Of these 70 million tons of steel, the United States produces one-third, Britain produces one-tenth, and Germany produces one-tenth. As for the recent example of Soviet Russia, it used to produce less than two percent, but now its production has reached six percent. Japan's production accounts for four percent. But things are not always favorable. Japan's steel industry began at the same time as China's—that is, more than 30 years ago. During the Guangxu era, Zhang Zhidong established a steel and iron plant in Hanyang, and at the same time, Japan built the Yawata steel plant near Moji. Although Japan has abundant coal, it has little that can be used for steelmaking, and it also lacks iron sand. At this time, China happened to be establishing a steel plant, which was very expensive. Japan took advantage of this and signed a contract with China. China used the money from Japan to establish the steel furnace. Because of the long-term contract, Japan did not have to worry about the shortage of iron sand. In the second year of the Republic, the contract was revised, requiring the Hanyeping company to supply Japan with 35 million tons of iron sand, but the entire mine only contained 30 million tons. In addition, there is a mine in Fanshan County, Anhui Province, which also signed a long-term iron sand sales contract with Japan, selling the entire mine completely. Therefore, according to statistics, the iron ore sold to the Japanese along the Yangtze River amounts to more than 20 million tons. As far as China is concerned, the output is only 100 million tons, of which 20 million tons have already been sold, and a large amount is being transported to foreign countries, which is truly alarming. Of the 100 million tons of iron ore produced in China, there are 71 million tons in Liaoning, which is even more frightening. How can we make full use of the remaining 29 million tons? This is a very big question. Before the war, Japan's steel production was only 3 million tons, while China's was only 50,000 tons. Now, they produce 3 million tons, while China produces less than 1,000 tons, and the steel plants have all been shut down. This comparison makes us even more afraid. India's situation is similar to China's, but when we started using new-style steelmaking, they were still using old methods. In the eighth year of the Republic, when China established the Longyan steel plant, they also established the Tata steel plant. We hired Americans to design it, and they also hired Americans to design it. But now they can produce 1 million tons of pig iron, at a very low cost, and it is entirely managed by the Indians themselves. As for us, the Longyan steel plant was successfully built, but it has never been fired up, which is truly shameful. Originally, China attached great importance to the iron and steel policy. Now, we must first promote the establishment of steel plants ourselves, and second, the export of iron sand should be managed by the government. No matter who sells iron sand to foreigners, the time should not be too long, and the quantity should be carefully considered, so that it can supply our own steelmaking.

Tungsten. China produces the most tungsten ore in the world, and it is famous for its rich tungsten production. It is said that China's tungsten production accounts for 80% of the world's total. In the past eight years, there have been considerable changes. In the most recent year, its production accounts for about 60% of the world's total. The use of tungsten is very limited in peacetime, mainly used to make lead type. However, in wartime, the use of tungsten is particularly large. Because its melting point is very high, it is an indispensable material for making military instruments such as armor-piercing bullets. The price of tungsten can be used to gauge the danger of the international situation, like a barometer. The higher the price of tungsten, the more dangerous the international situation. The lower the price of tungsten, the less likely a major crisis will occur. The world's tungsten production is more than 16,000 tons, and China's is 12,000 tons, accounting for three-quarters. Although the production is large, the situation is not reassuring. China's tungsten smelting can produce 99.97% pure tungsten, but the new smelting technology can achieve 99.99%. Mexico is now using new smelting technology, and the Americans are selling it to China's competitors. Now the government is considering establishing a bureau to deal with this situation.

Tin. Tin is rarely used in peacetime. Its main use is to add it to iron for steelmaking. However, modern weapons cannot do without tin; without tin, they will suffer losses. The main tin-producing countries in the world are China and Burma. The world's total tin production is 140,000 tons, of which China accounts for 60,000 tons and Burma accounts for 50,000 tons. If China does not seek progress, Burma will soon catch up. The global sale of tin is mainly in the hands of the British and Chinese governments. China currently does not have the capital to make good use of it. Britain can sell it for a long time, and the United States, Germany, Japan, and Italy must buy it from Britain and China. However, the sale of tin is closely related to other countries, and it cannot be compared to ordinary commercial transactions. The British Armstrong Company once asked the Chinese government to transfer the right to sell tin to Britain. Fortunately, this negotiation did not succeed. We should prioritize the interests of the country and support it well, because it is closely related to military affairs and politics.

Coal and Oil. In addition to factories, cars and airplanes need gasoline; gasoline is refined from oil. Countries without oil will face great difficulties with gasoline in wartime. For example, in the Abyssinian War, the League of Nations imposed an oil embargo. If implemented, Italy would have faced great difficulties. Therefore, oil deposits are extremely important. Japan uses more than 2.2 million tons of oil annually, of which 470,000 tons are used by the navy. Japan can supply more than 200,000 tons itself, Taiwan supplies 300,000 tons, Karafuto 300,000 tons, and Liaoning Fushun 100,000 tons, totaling 900,000 to 670,000 tons. The difference of 1.7 million tons is imported: 1 million tons from the United States and 700,000 tons from Southeast Asia. As for the accumulation of oil, we can estimate the reserves. According to estimates by Americans and Russians, Japan's oil reserves are 400,000 to 670,000 tons, enough for about one year of use. Not only oil, but also copper and iron are like this. Japan produces 3 million tons of steel annually, and in addition to buying iron sand from China, Korea, and Malaya, it imports 4 million tons. Japan produces only 200,000 tons itself, and the rest is imported from foreign countries. Japan's iron sand reserves are 9 million tons. Therefore, a country must pay attention to necessary resources not only in wartime, but also in peacetime. Otherwise, it will face great difficulties when the time comes. The League of Nations' collective security and non-aggression treaty requires countries at war to deal with it, and countries not at war must also deal with it. Therefore, buying from foreign countries in wartime is not easy, so we must prepare in peacetime.

All countries in the world attach great importance to mineral resources. Everyone is working hard in two directions: one is to vigorously improve the production of their own country, and the other is to facilitate the supply from foreign countries, such as signing contracts and treaties. In China's situation, especially with regard to iron sand and steel, we must pay special attention to their disposition. We must develop it and protect it, and we should pay special attention to the greenness of important mineral resources. On the one hand, we should promote international trade, but on the other hand, we should also store up our own strength. To stand in the world, we must have considerable strength. This kind of strength comes from two sources: people and land. People must do their best, and the land must be used to its full potential. Only by using the power of people to develop the riches of the land can the country begin to develop its power.

川行散記 85

— Travel Notes from Sichuan

— Record of Hardships

2 Chongqing Escape

Chongqing sits at the confluence of the Yangtze and Jialing Rivers. During the Spring and Autumn Period, it was the capital of the Ba Kingdom. Under the Qin Dynasty, it became Ba Commandery. The Tang Dynasty called it Yu Prefecture, and the Song Dynasty renamed it Chongqing in support of a new beginning. This is a city on a hillside, surrounded by water on three sides, forming a peninsula. Fifteen miles west of the city is the Fotu Pass, which controls the throat of the ancient Chengdu-Chongqing route, the closest point between the two rivers before they merged. The Fotu Pass is a narrow and precipitous cliff, a strategic location that was a battleground for military strategists. The mountain is narrow and long, resembling a goose's neck, while the city resembles the goose's body. If you were to use Shanghai's Huangpu River and Suzhou Creek as a comparison, then the Wenbei district on the north bank of the Jialing River would be Zhabei, and the south bank across the Yangtze River would be like Pudong. In terms of topography, they are also quite similar. The north bank is a less developed area in terms of material civilization, while the south bank is the rural area that nurtures the prosperity of the city.

The city's streets rise and fall with the terrain, and the buildings are constructed at varying heights. There are stone steps going up and down slopes, as well as modern roads. There are dilapidated mansions and the latest Western-style buildings. The means of transportation are both old and new. It is not uncommon to see antique sedan chairs and streamlined 1936 automobiles running side by side on the streets. Public buses are very developed, but unfortunately, they are not well managed. The rear of the buses emits plumes of black smoke, forcing pedestrians to cover their noses and hurry past. Sedan chairs are a type of covered litter, the only means of transportation for narrow and remote alleys where cars cannot pass. There is also a type called "big sedan chair," which is a high-backed sedan chair carried by four or six people taking turns. It is made with delicate rattan chairs, and the ends of the sedan poles are extra long, making it more stable when going uphill or downhill. These are privately owned by wealthy or obese individuals. Every time I see these sedan chairs, with servants shouting and clearing the way, rushing ahead, the pomp and circumstance often arouse in me the "he could be replaced by me" sense of decline. Indeed, a wealthy person in Chongqing would rather have a big sedan chair than a cheap car. Cars are just a toy.

The municipal management seems too poor. Compared with Qingdao and Hong Kong, which have similar situations and are also mountain cities, there is a vast difference. Vehicles on the roads originally drove on the right, but later, with the implementation of the New Life Movement, they were changed to the left. Now, even a very narrow pedestrian path is divided into left and right halves for separate traffic. Public utilities, besides the smoke-belching buses, include streetlights, telephones, toll-free radio stations, and tap water with stations for selling water. There is also a park, but it is not as good as any of the private villas owned by military officers along the Jialing River.

Chongqing University is the only institution of higher learning in Chongqing, founded single-handedly by Chairman Liu Xiang. It has only been around for four years, so naturally, one cannot criticize its facilities using conventional standards. However, its campus on the banks of the Jialing River is beautiful and secluded, truly an excellent place for studying. If calculated per capita, Chongqing probably has more secondary schools than Shanghai, with a total number of over thirty. Primary schools are even more developed, and traditional private schools continue to operate. Naturally, with so many schools, there is a high demand for teachers. However, there are even more people eager to become teachers, leading to the so-called "Sixth and Twelfth Month Wars" – the activities of the education sector during the winter and summer vacations. The term of office for principals, except for missionary schools and a very few private schools, is usually no more than one academic year. Teachers are not considered full-time or part-time but are merely a token response to the recommendation letters of influential people by the principal. A close friend of mine teaches at four secondary schools that are very far apart, teaching over forty-two hours per week. I asked him how he manages to teach so much. He told me a clever trick to be in many places at once: he takes a week off from each school in rotation each month, so he can handle it with ease.

Chongqing is an economic center and a military center. Officials, politicians, merchants, and the wealthy are all active there. To meet their needs, hotels, restaurants, theaters, and all the other pleasures that a metropolis should provide are extremely developed. Dumei Street is Chongqing's Nanjing Road, a gathering place for department stores and the business hub for foreign merchants. If you walk into a store, the clerks will point to the goods and tell you, "This is from Shanghai, this is Jiangnan goods." The so-called Shanghai or Jiangnan goods are mostly Western goods.

Sichuan opera mostly uses Qin melodies, with loud, sonorous, and exciting tunes that people from Jiangdong find boring. Sichuan cuisine, on the other hand, is most famous for the Chengdu flavor. The characteristics of Sichuan cuisine are oiliness, spiciness, sourness, and tenderness. Most dishes are stir-fried with heavy oil and immediately served, without stewing. Chongqing's currents are swift, making it difficult to find aquatic products. Carp is considered a delicacy, and shrimp and crabs are even rarer. Pork is an essential main dish for every meal, while preserved meat and sausages are the only common household foods. If you want to eat yellow croaker or mandarin fish, it is truly "a horseshoe crab hanging from your nose" (an impossibility). Therefore, outsiders who come to Sichuan for the first time often lament "no fish to eat," and Sichuan people get used to eating oily food. Breakfast is the most important meal of the day for them, so they don't pay much attention to snacks. Lunch is called "Xiangwu" (midday meal), and dinner is called "Xiaoye" (late-night snack), suggesting that they are more important. Especially for children, because adults want them to go to bed early, they often prefer a late-night snack. The time for banquets is usually set for two or three in the afternoon, but in reality, they must wait until six or seven o'clock before they can begin.

Sichuan has always been known as the "Land of Abundance," with many special products. The white fungus produced in the deep mountains on the border of Sichuan and Guizhou is highly praised, with large, white, slightly yellow ones being the best. The snow-white ones on the Shanghai market, although beautiful, are of inferior quality. Jiading silk and Chengdu brocade are famous products, sold in shops around Shaanxi Street.

Page 10

Gansu Provincial Government Relieves Rural Spring Planting 86

Organizing a Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee

Nominating Deng Baoshan and Four Others as Committee Members

Lanzhou Correspondence: Provincial Government Chairman Yu Xuezhong, in view of the fact that the province suffered more severe disasters and bandit disturbances last year, and that there is an urgent need for relief, specifically proposed at the 383rd Provincial Affairs Meeting to organize a Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee and overdraft 500,000 yuan from the bank as relief funds. The proposal was approved, and Deng Baoshan, Zhang Wei, Liu Guangpei, Zhu Jingzhou, and Gu Zude were nominated as committee members, with Liu Guangpei as the chairman. The committee's various regulations have been drafted separately. The original text is as follows:

Organizational Regulations Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee Organizational Regulations, Article 1: The Gansu Provincial Government, in order to relieve farmers in disaster areas during spring planting and prevent high-interest loans, organizes a Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee. Article 2: The committee consists of five to seven members, with one chairman, all nominated by the Provincial Government Committee. Article 3: The committee has three executive officers, each appointed by the Department of Civil Affairs, the Department of Finance, and the Farmers Bank, to handle documents, accounting, investigation, and other matters. It also employs a number of staff members, allocated by the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance. Article 4: The committee may establish sub-committees in disaster-stricken counties, the general rules for which will be determined separately. Article 5: The powers of the committee are as follows: Matters concerning disaster area investigation; Matters concerning loan allocation and recovery; Matters concerning the guidance and supervision of sub-committees. Article 6: All committee staff members serve on a voluntary basis. Article 7: When the committee sends personnel to various counties for investigation, the necessary travel expenses shall be paid by the provincial government in accordance with the province's travel expense regulations. Article 8: The committee's loan rules will be determined separately. Article 9: The committee's address is located within the provincial government. Article 10: These regulations shall come into effect on the date of promulgation and may be amended at any time if there are any omissions.

General Rules for Sub-Committees Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee Sub-Committee Organizational General Rules, Article 1: These general rules are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of the Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee Organizational Regulations. Article 2: Each county sub-committee shall have five to seven members, who shall be composed of the following personnel: The county magistrate; One standing committee member of the County Rectification Committee; One member of the County Farmers Association; Two to four local impartial individuals selected by the county government. One chairman shall be appointed, concurrently held by the county magistrate. Article 3: Each county sub-committee shall have three executive officers and a number of staff members, all appointed concurrently by the chairman from local government agencies, and reported to the Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee for record. Article 4: All county sub-committee service personnel serve on a voluntary basis. Article 5: The powers of the county sub-committee are as follows: Matters concerning disaster area investigation; Matters concerning loan income and distribution; Matters concerning loan recovery. Article 6: In order to ensure loan repayment and establish a foundation for mutual economic assistance among farmers, the county sub-committee must first order disaster-stricken farmers to organize a cooperative preparatory society, and then provide loans. The organizational charter shall be determined separately. Article 7: When the county sub-committee sends personnel to disaster areas for investigation, the necessary travel expenses shall be economized from local public funds and shall not be apportioned separately. Investigating personnel shall not accept supplies from local farmers. Article 8: The address of the county sub-committee shall be located within the county government. Article 9: These general rules shall come into effect on the date of approval and promulgation, and may be submitted for amendment at any time if there are any omissions.

Loan Rules Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee Loan Rules, Article 1: These rules are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 8 of the Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee Organizational Regulations. Article 2: The loan affairs of this committee in various counties shall be managed by the Rural Spring Planting Relief Sub-Committees of each county (hereinafter referred to as the "Sub-Committees"). Article 3: The loans of this committee shall only be issued to rural cooperative preparatory societies (hereinafter referred to as the "Preparatory Societies") approved by the Sub-Committees. Article 4: The loans of this committee shall be calculated at a monthly interest rate of two per cent. Article 5: The repayment period for the loans of this committee is ten months. Article 6: The loans borrowed by members shall only be used for the purchase of seeds, agricultural tools, livestock, and fertilizers. Article 7: When members of the Preparatory Society borrow loans from the Preparatory Society, they shall fill out a loan application form and submit it to the chairman of the Preparatory Society. The chairman shall collect the loan application forms of all members and submit them to the appraisal committee for review and determination. Article 8: When the Preparatory Society requests a loan from the County Sub-Committee, it shall fill out three copies of a list of all members and submit them to the Sub-Committee (stating the member's name, age, address, loan amount, and loan purpose), and obtain a loan form and loan contract from the County Sub-Committee, fill them out separately, and submit them to the County Sub-Committee. After receiving the aforementioned forms and tables, the County Sub-Committee shall send personnel to investigate and report back before making a decision. Article 9: The maximum loan amount for each member shall not exceed thirty yuan. Article 10: The County Sub-Committee shall order the Preparatory Society to fill out three copies of the loan contract, one copy to be kept by the County Sub-Committee, one copy to be kept by the Preparatory Society, and the County Sub-Committee shall forward it to the Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee along with the member list for record. Article 11: If the Preparatory Society borrowing the loan repays it before the due date, the interest shall be calculated up to the date of repayment. Article 12: If, after issuing the loan, the County Sub-Committee discovers that the Preparatory Society borrowing the loan has used it improperly or engaged in other fraudulent activities, it may immediately order the repayment of the loan principal and interest, and reorganize or cancel the Preparatory Society. Article 13: If the staff of the County Sub-Committee or the Preparatory Society are found to have engaged in embezzlement, corruption of loans, or favoritism, they shall be severely punished according to law, in addition to recovering the embezzled funds. Article 14: When the County Sub-Committee's loans have reached the total loan amount allocated to the county, it may announce the cessation of lending. Article 15: These rules shall come into effect on the date of approval, and may be submitted for amendment at any time if there are any omissions.

Preparatory Society Charter

Gansu Province Rural Cooperative Preparatory Society Provisional Regulations, Article 1: This Preparatory Society is established in accordance with the provisions of Article 6 of the Gansu Province Spring Planting Relief Committee County Sub-Committee Organizational General Rules. Article 2: This Preparatory Society is named the County, District, Village Cooperative Preparatory Society. Article 3: This Preparatory Society aims to restore the agriculture of its members through the spirit of self-help and mutual assistance, in order to promote the formation of a formal rural cooperative, and to first handle spring planting relief matters. Article 4: All members of this Preparatory Society bear joint and several unlimited liability. Article 5: The business area of this Preparatory Society is Village, and the office is located in Village. Article 6: The period of existence of this Preparatory Society is temporarily set at one year. Article 7: Any citizen of the Republic of China, regardless of gender, who is at least twenty years old, resides within the area of this society, and has the following qualifications may become a member: Holding the position of head of household; Having independent living ability; Obtaining proof from the local Baojia chief; Must borrow loans in order to carry out spring planting. Article 8: Anyone with one of the following circumstances may not be a member of this Preparatory Society: Having bad habits; Having been a coerced follower of the communists and having actively worked for them without surrendering. If a member of this Preparatory Society is found to have one of the aforementioned circumstances, the member may be expelled by a resolution of the general meeting of members. Article 9: Members of this Preparatory Society may not simultaneously be members of other preparatory societies. Article 10: Members of this Preparatory Society may enjoy the right to borrow loans from this Preparatory Society in accordance with the provisions of the Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee Loan Rules. Article 11: If a member of this Preparatory Society withdraws from the society due to leaving or other reasons, they must repay their individual debts to the society. In the event of death, the debt shall be repaid by their heirs. Article 12: The officers of this Preparatory Society are as follows: One president, who manages all affairs of the society; One vice-president, who assists the president in handling affairs; One treasurer, who manages the receipt and disbursement of funds; One clerk, who manages documents. The aforementioned officers shall be elected by the general meeting of members. Their term of office shall last until the expiration of the society's existence. In the event of a vacancy, a replacement shall be elected at any time. Article 13: This Preparatory Society shall establish an appraisal committee, composed of three to seven members elected by the general meeting of members, who shall elect one member as chairman. The appraisal committee shall have the power to supervise all affairs of this Preparatory Society and mediate disputes among members. Article 14: The general meeting of members shall be held once every three months and shall be convened by the president. Extraordinary meetings may be convened when necessary. Article 16: All officers of this Preparatory Society serve on a voluntary basis. Article 17: At the end of the existence of this Preparatory Society, if there is a surplus after settlement, it shall be transferred as start-up funds and public reserve funds for the reorganization of a rural credit cooperative. Article 18: This charter shall be implemented after being approved by the County Rural Spring Planting Relief Sub-Committee and reported to the Gansu Province Rural Spring Planting Relief Committee for record after being passed by the general meeting of members.

Smuggling Organizations in Southern Fujian 87

The Main Office is Located in Xiamen

Branch Offices are Established Throughout the Interior

Xiamen Correspondence: Tax evasion and smuggling are extremely prevalent in Xiamen and the coastal areas of southern Fujian. Since the Third Pacification Command destroyed the Nan Shun Foreign Firm, a smuggling organization operating out of Shilian Town outside the South Gate of Quanzhou, smugglers in Jinjiang and Hui'an have been losing their nerve, either suspending operations or relocating to conceal their activities. According to recent news from Quanzhou, the smuggling organizations established by unscrupulous merchants actually have their headquarters in Xiamen, with branch offices in Zhangzha of Hui'an, Tatao of Anhai, and Shijing of Jinjiang. Most of the key members are from Takku of Hui'an. Because Hui'an is located on the coast, close to Taiwan, and many residents make a living by sailing, no fewer than three hundred people have been relying on smuggling for their livelihood since the commencement of smuggling operations. The main office in Xiamen is located on Kaiyuan Road, formed by four foreign firms with a capital of over 500,000 yuan. Their smuggling routes depart from a small island near Taiwan, transshipping to the coastal areas of Jinjiang, Nan'an, and Hui'an, with well-fortified storage rooms (i.e., smuggled goods warehouses) along the way and a wide network of informants to prevent detection. They have established radio stations for communication. Even if there is a leak, it is difficult to completely crack down. It is said that the main company was established in 1934, and its initial scale was small. After the horizontal announcement of the implementation of legal tender last year, the company made huge profits by smuggling silver, and then expanded its organization and established branch offices throughout the interior. According to those familiar with the situation, Zeng Moujie, who was captured in Shishi, was the general manager of the branch offices in the Quanzhou area, directing the loading and unloading of goods in various branch offices. Zhuang Yankui was the contact person for the main company in Xiamen, responsible for public relations and liaison. He happened to be dispatched by the main company to Shishi to negotiate, so he was also arrested. The staff of the main company in Xiamen have already fled one after another. Quanzhou is currently temporarily entrusted to a certain dentist to preside over the affairs, intending to first find a way to rescue the detainees. They have been sending people to Quanzhou for activities in recent days. The authorities attach great importance to this matter and are making every effort to investigate. (March 15)

Travel Notes from Hubei and Guangdong (None) (Travel Correspondence from Our Newspaper Reporter) A Trip to the South 88

— Zhao Junhao

Since arriving in Wuhan on the second of this month, it has been five days today (the sixth). Every day has been shrouded in haze, and I have not seen the sun once. A friend told me that it rains frequently in Hunan Province, and there are rainy days for more than two-thirds of the year. If it is overcast and there is no sunlight, it can already be considered a sunny day. You should consider yourself lucky and not be dissatisfied. On the morning of the sixth, we took bamboo sedan chairs to tour the mountains. First, we went to the Zhisheng Temple, a magnificent building with ancient, verdant trees. After lingering for a while, we left. After exiting the temple, the sedan chair carriers, seeing my weight, asked to add another carrier, jokingly saying to me, "You are very lucky." I did not understand their meaning at first, but after Mr. Zhong Shusheng told me the reason, I couldn't help but smile! After leaving Zhisheng Temple, we saw many paddy fields along the way. A stream meandered through the rocks, and we gradually heard the sound of water, like thunder. After half an hour, we arrived at the Water Curtain Cave, a waterfall that plunged down from a great height. It is said that its source is on Mount Zhurong. The waterfall is not wide, but it is light and bright like a curtain. On a large rock next to the waterfall are engraved the words "Unceasing Day and Night," "High Mountains and Flowing Water," and "Where to Go and Where to Come." After touring the Water Curtain Cave, we traveled for some time to Nanyue City. The so-called Nanyue City is the street market in front of the Nanyue Temple. It is said that since the Tang and Song Dynasties, those who visited the mountains and burned incense have stopped here. Over time, it became prosperous and developed into a city. There are various shops in the city, and many old-fashioned hotels. During July and August, pilgrims from all over the world come to Nanyue to offer incense, and most of the hotels are full. From here, we entered the Nanyue Temple, a magnificent temple comparable to the Lingyin Temple in Hangzhou. The aisle is very long, with rows of pine and cypress trees, which is extremely beautiful. The most special thing is that the main hall is surrounded by a long corridor. The construction method is the same as that of the palaces in the ancient capital of Beiping. The long corridor is surrounded by stone railings, and the stone slabs of the railings are all carved with trees, flowers, and birds, all of which are exquisite. It is said that the total number of pilgrims who come here every year is more than 200,000, and many people from the Jiangzhe area, such as Shanghai, Suzhou, and Hangzhou, also go there, which can be said to be a grand occasion. After the Nanyue Temple, we climbed the mountain. The mountain roads are all newly built roads, which are very easy to walk. The situation is the same as the new roads on Mount Mogan. However, looking at the snow-capped mountain peaks in the distance, the cold wind hit us, and we shivered in the sedan chairs. After walking for a short time, we arrived at Luosi Pool, another waterfall, with a loud sound of water. The waterfall folds several times, which is more beautiful than the Water Curtain Cave. After advancing from here, we passed the Jade Plate Bridge. The terrain became higher, and the climate became colder. It was much colder than the coldest winter weather in Shanghai. At that time, snowflakes were floating, and we couldn't stand the cold and cried out in pain. After moving forward for several miles, we finally reached Banshan Pavilion, which is halfway from the foot of the mountain to the top. We went to the China Travel Service Hostel, gathered around the stove for dinner, and the cold was greatly reduced. There are more than a dozen rooms here, which is the best place in the whole mountain. It is not inferior to Mount Lu for summering, and it will be open this summer. After dinner, because the weather was cold and the road was slippery, and the snow had not stopped, we could not go up further, so we took another new road down the sunny side of the mountain. Because this section faces the sun, there are more trees, and the scenery is gradually better. On the way, we passed the Mogging Terrace, and nearby is a villa built by He Jian, Chairman of Hunan Province. Further down, we toured Fuyan Temple and Nantai Temple, both of which are built on the mountain and have excellent environments. Nantai Temple also has more than 5,000 volumes of Tibetan scriptures sent by Japanese monks, stored in a small building's bookcase, with a stone tablet recording the event. In addition, there are thirty-two Buddha images on palm leaves, with exquisite workmanship, which are masterpieces. We then went down the mountain and still went to the Travel Service Hostel at the foot of the mountain for a short rest.

Overall, the beauty of Nanyue lies in its breadth, grandeur, and wonder. The temples and historical sites are scattered everywhere and cannot be compared to those that can be seen all at once. The mountain is more than 3,000 feet high, which is very suitable for summering. In addition, the Hunan Provincial Government has set up a bureau to manage everything, so the future is promising. Those who come from Hankou can take a car from Changsha to the mountain, and those who come from Guangdong can change trains from Hengyang to the mountain. After a short rest at the Travel Service, we were accompanied by Director Yang Yufen of the Zhushao Bureau and took a car to Hengyang, which took two hours to reach. We crossed the river outside Hengyang City to the east bank of the river and stayed at Mr. Yang's residence.

Travelogue of Qinghai (Continued) 89

— Zhuang Xueben

The Locals are Mongols

We can now conclude that the ethnicity of the Qinghai natives is of Mongol origin:

In the past, some people said that they were descendants of Li Keyong of the Shatuo State. The so-called Shatuo State—is the present-day Shatuo in Xinjiang; northwest of Dihua, Suilai, Fukang, Fuyuan, Qitai counties, five hundred li in length and three hundred li in width, now called Gurbantunggut Desert. The Tang Dynasty called it Shatuo. It is east of Pulei, and south of Jinpo Mountain, belonging to a separate part of the Western Turkic Khaganate. Later it was attached to the Uyghurs. — This theory exists because Li Tusi is a descendant of Li Keyong, but this only applies to a small number of nobles and cannot be attributed to the majority of the indigenous people. Moreover, many of the Tusi are Mongols or from Jiangnan. Checking the genealogy of the Li Tusi, since the Yuan Dynasty, the Mei brothers Guguan Luji divided the Hongyagou territory, and in the Ming Dynasty, the Li Ying and Li Xiong brothers were granted the titles of Marquis of Huining and Earl of Gaoyang, which were hereditary. At that time, they were all called native people, and now the people of Qinghai also call them Turen, so it is very clear that they are genuine Qinghai natives, not immigrants from elsewhere.

Now the Xizhuang people call them "Kalong," and they call themselves "Mongol Er." Their language is Mongolian. They have great and strong builds, yellow skin, black pupils, and thick lips. Their neighbors are also close to the Mongols. These few significant features can prove that they are a branch of the Mongolian ethnicity.

In the past, they had a glorious war history with their Tusi, and they all contributed to the suppression of border disturbances in the Western Regions in previous dynasties. Because they used to be good at martial arts, their culture is now backward, and they are lazy to cultivate. However, they have loyal personalities, strong physiques, intelligent minds, and beautiful faces. If the government can provide appropriate education, they can restore their past glory.

Statistics of Native People

The above is based on the county government's survey in the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1933], totaling more than 5,800 people. Recent population figures are not available.

Besides being centered in Huzhu County, the Qinghai natives also live scattered in Datong, Xining, Gonghe, Minhe, Ledu, and five other counties. However, most have been sinicized and are difficult to distinguish. The total number of natives in Qinghai Province is estimated by the author to be about 20,000 to 30,000.

Huzhu County Tusi

Li Tusi (see previous chapter 6)

Dongqi Tusi (see previous chapter 13)

Xiqi Tusi is of Mongolian ethnicity. In the fourth year of Hongwu in the Ming Dynasty, Nanmu Ge led craftsmen to surrender and was awarded the title of Commander Qian Shi for his merits. His grandson Zaifu was promoted to Commander for his merits. By the time of his ninth-generation grandson, Zaidengyuan, after resigning from his post in the 24th year of Wanli, he was promoted to the garrison commander of Tumun Fort. In the early Qing Dynasty, Chengyuan's son Wang Shenglong surrendered in the second year of Shunzhi and inherited the position of Commander Qian Shi in the fourth year. Later generations inherited the position. Now he lives in Haizigou, forty li west of Xining County, and the natives of Huzhu County are under his jurisdiction.

Na Tusi is of Mongolian ethnicity. In the fourth year of Hongwu in the Ming Dynasty, Shami led his tribe to surrender and was awarded the title of General Flag. Shami's son, Nasula, was promoted to Deputy Thousand Household in the first year of Yongle for his merits. By the time of his sixth-generation grandson, Na Rong, he inherited the position during the Jiajing period and was promoted to Commander Qian Shi for his merits. By the time of his ninth-generation grandson, Na Ruyan, after inheriting the position in the 31st year of Wanli, he was promoted to Guerrilla of the Guyuan Standard. In the early Qing Dynasty, Na Ruyan's son, Na Yuanbiao, surrendered in the second year of Shunzhi and inherited the position of Commander Qian Shi in the tenth year. Later generations inherited the position. Now he lives in Najiazhuang, twelve li south of Xining County, and is now residing in Xichuan. The natives of Najia Dongyuan and other villages under the jurisdiction of Huzhu County are there.

Chen Tusi is originally from Shanyang, Jiangnan. His ancestor, Chen Ziming, was the Right Vice Minister of Huai'an during the Yuan Dynasty. In the first year of Hongwu in the Ming Dynasty, he was awarded the title of Commander. Ziming's son, Chen Yi, inherited the position in the 17th year of Hongwu and was transferred to the Xining Guard Commander for his merits. By the time of his sixth-generation grandson, Chen Zhi, he inherited the position and also managed the military affairs of the camp. Later, he died in battle and was posthumously awarded the title of Deputy Commander-in-Chief. By the time of his tenth-generation grandson, Chen Guangxian, he inherited the position during the Wanli period and was promoted to Left Assistant General of Zhuanglang. In the early Qing Dynasty, Chen Guangxian's son, Chen Shiwen, surrendered in the second year of Shunzhi and inherited the position of Commander in the ninth year. He was promoted to Niangou Garrison Commander for his merits. Later generations inherited the position. Now he lives in Chenjiatai, in the western district of Huzhu County.

Ji Tusi is of Mongolian ethnicity. There was Ji Bao who surrendered in the early years of Hongwu in the Ming Dynasty and was awarded the title of Hundred Household and transferred to the Zhenfu of the Jinyi Guard's former institute. By the time of his grandson, Jixiang, he inherited the position in the 20th year of Yongle and was promoted to Commander Qian Shi for his merits. In the early Qing Dynasty, Ji Tianxi surrendered in the second year of Shunzhi and inherited the hereditary position of Commander Qian Shi in the twelfth year. He lives in Jijiazhuang, sixty li west of Xining County. (The above is taken from "Recent Qinghai One")

Reactionary Criminals Receive Separate Sentences

More than ten reactionary criminals, including Zhou Jizeng, were captured by the Jiangsu Provincial Public Security Office and sent to the Jiangsu Higher Court for trial. The Higher Court has repeatedly interrogated them and concluded the trial. The judgment was announced yesterday: Zhou Zongpei was sentenced to 15 years of imprisonment for organizing a group with the aim of harming the Republic of China; Lin Liying was sentenced to 10 years; Guan Yongkuan and Wang Ziming were each sentenced to 7 years; Wang Ganqing was sentenced to 5 years; Wang Jihui and Wang Xiuhua were each sentenced to 3 years; Hang Zhengdao was sentenced to 2 years and 6 months; Communist Party printed materials and newspapers were confiscated.

Murdering Police Officer Appeals to High Court

Patrol Officer Hong Shiqin and five patrolmen including He of the Fifth Precinct of the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau jointly murdered Gu Agen. The District Court sentenced He Naikang to death, Hong Shi to ten years of imprisonment, and the others were sentenced separately. He Naikang and Hong Shiqin refused to accept the judgment and appealed to the Higher Court. The appeal has been approved and accepted, and the trial is scheduled to begin tomorrow (17th). He has hired lawyer Yao Xiaoqiu to appear in court to defend him at that time.

Theft Case Quickly Solved

Changshu, 14th: An unprecedented robbery occurred here this afternoon. Fortunately, the victim vigorously pursued the thief. The victim, Chen Quan, employed by Ji Guoping's family in Zhong Sheng Lane, was ordered to withdraw 900 yuan in foreign currency from the Bank of China this afternoon. The money had been eyed by criminals. When Chen Quan arrived at a small alley in Zhong Sheng Lane, Chen Quan was violently struck in the face by a large man, Chen fainted and fell to the ground. The man then stole the banknotes and fled. However, Chen, due to the money being stolen, endured the pain and chased after him, shouting for the thief to be caught. Unexpectedly, the thief was also in a hurry and came up with an idea, blowing his own police whistle wildly, falsely reporting a fire. When he reached Mutou Lane, a rickshaw puller and a tailor happened to be coming from the opposite direction and captured him. Fortunately, the stolen items were not scattered. He was then sent to the Public Security Bureau. The thief confessed his name as Chen Youbin, a resident of the city, and claimed that there was a misunderstanding along the way and that he was not robbing. Because the authorities considered this case to be an unprecedented daylight robbery case that was quickly solved, they are paying close attention to it. It will be handed over to the county for investigation on the 16th, which is a Saturday.

Various Industries Rectify Accumulated Grain and Solicit Donations

Jiaxing: The Jiaxing County Government has promulgated interim measures for raising accumulated grain, stipulating the amount of grain that shops should donate. The public offices in various towns have begun to solicit donations. However, when dispatching personnel to solicit donations from various shops, they do not follow the measures issued by the county government, and the starting capital amount does not follow the capital declared in the original business tax. They often forcibly increase the amount, exceeding the quota, causing repeated complaints. Various shops have reported this to their respective trade associations, and the trade associations have jointly requested the County Chamber of Commerce to come forward and preside over the matter, striving for the authorities to continue to follow Article 7 of the interim measures, which stipulates that the capital of the merchant Tang Dynasty should be based on the records of the Business Tax Bureau when soliciting accumulated grain, so as to comply with the law. After receiving the report, the County Chamber of Commerce has requested the County Magistrate to instruct the public offices of various towns to comply with it.

Su-Jia Road Adds Branch Line

The Su-Jia Railway is scheduled to open to traffic on May 1st. Currently, the railway tracks are being laid, and the foundations of the four and six bridges on the Jiaxing section are not very solid, so they are being dismantled and rebuilt. According to reliable sources, the railway will also open a route from Sinai in Jiaxing County to connect to the Ma Huang Tang Bridge, so the Ma Huang Tang Bridge area needs to be opened as a branch station. The line is currently being surveyed by the engineering office.

Agricultural Bank Adds Five Offices

Hangzhou: The China Farmers Bank has recently transferred 300,000 yuan in new banknotes to Hangzhou for circulation in the market. It is reported that the bank plans to add offices in Jiangshan, Ningbo, Wenzhou, Wu Yu, and five other locations in order to help rural areas develop their businesses. It will explore establishing them first and starting business operations.
