Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank 1935 Business Overview 134

Adopting a Policy of Solidifying Reserves as a Business Strategy

Currency Reform Strengthens Foreign Exchange Business

Handling Rural Loans Progresses Smoothly

Central News Agency reports that the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank held a board meeting yesterday to report on past business and future business strategies. The following details the bank's 1935 business overview and service overview.

Business Overview The bank's business policy for this year, in light of the adverse environment, has consistently focused on solidifying reserves. Indeed, the primary duty of a bank serving society is to protect the interests of its depositors. Given the unstable financial market this year, and to further strengthen the protection of depositors, the bank has sought to increase its cash reserves. Consequently, it has been necessary to moderately restrict assistance to industrial and commercial enterprises compared to times of peace. At the end of this year, the total loan and cash reserve balance is as stated in the current balance sheet, totaling over 130 million yuan. This includes over 57.7 million yuan in current deposits, over 42.6 million yuan in fixed deposits, and over 31.5 million yuan in savings deposits. All figures are lower than at the end of 1934, due to financial panic this year, with extreme anxiety among the public, which was reflected in deposit withdrawals, almost as a matter of course. Simultaneously, enterprise deposits experienced significant withdrawals as companies sought to meet their own needs due to market tension. Furthermore, to maintain sound operations in recent years, more than ten branches, offices, and agencies have been closed, which has also reduced deposits. Therefore, deposits have generally declined throughout the year, only ceasing after currency reform and then showing a trend of increase. At the end of this year, the total cash reserve was over 40.16 million yuan, an increase over the previous year. At the end of the previous year, the cash-to-deposit ratio was 21%, while at the end of this year it was 30%. Since the bank's business policy this year has focused on solidifying reserves, and the bank's loans have always been liquid, it has been easy to recover them despite the poor market conditions. The amount of loan repayments exceeds the amount of deposit decreases, and cash reserves have also increased accordingly. Loans and Investments At the end of this year, the total balance of loans, securities purchases, and real estate investments was over 120 million yuan, also a decrease from the previous year. This is a necessary step in solidifying reserves. Furthermore, stable industrial and commercial enterprises, aware of the adverse environment, are unwilling to make significant progress. The need for bank loans is not very strong. Activity only increased after currency reform. The total loan balance is over 100.2 million yuan, of which collateral loans account for 75%, credit loans account for 20%, and bills and discounts account for 5%. Among the collateral loans, commodity collateral accounts for more than half, followed by securities and factory collateral. The composition is similar to that of the previous year. The percentage of credit loans appears higher than in the previous year because the total loan amount in the previous year included securities purchases and real estate investments, while this year it does not. Therefore, the percentage appears higher, but in absolute terms, it is actually a 25% decrease from the previous year. Restrictions are very strict, and loans are only granted to customers with assured repayment, to protect the security of funds. In terms of investments, securities purchases at the end of this year were over 16 million yuan, and their book value is still lower than the market value. Real estate investments are mostly used for the bank's business and warehouse purposes. Accumulated depreciation has been applied in previous years, and the balance at the end of this year is over 8 million yuan. Profit and Distribution The total net profit for the year was over 844,400 yuan. The distribution method was resolved at the board meetings on July 26, 1935, and January 15, 1936, as follows:

A. Net profit for the year 844,939.63 yuan

Plus retained earnings from last year 3,018.01 yuan

Total 875,957.64 yuan

B. Distribution resolved by the board of directors in two phases:

1. Appropriation for public bonds 100,000.00 yuan

2. Payment of shareholder dividends at 5% 100,000.00 yuan 410,000.00 yuan

and a bonus of 4%

410,000.00 yuan

3. Appropriation for dividend reserve 50,000.00 yuan

4. Appropriation for remuneration for directors and supervisors 10,000.00 yuan

5. Appropriation for remuneration for general and deputy general manager-level employees 200,000.00 yuan

Balance carried forward to the next period 65,957.00 yuan

Total 875,957.64 yuan Loan contraction this year reduced interest income compared to the previous year, but exchange gains increased due to foreign exchange arbitrage and increased documentary bills. All expenses, amortizations, and write-offs are shown in the profit and loss statement, similar to the previous year. Write-offs are strictly handled to ensure the accuracy of assets. Reserves In this year, 100,000 yuan was appropriated for public reserve, and another 50,000 yuan was appropriated for dividend reserve in order to balance future dividend payments. The current public reserve totals 5.2 million yuan, and the operating reserve has increased to 2.3 million yuan. Including the dividend reserve, the total is 7.55 million yuan, exceeding the capital by 2.55 million yuan, further ensuring the interests of shareholders and depositors. Increase and Decrease of Branches Given the adverse environment this year, and for the sake of centralized management and sound operations, branches, offices, or agencies with mediocre performance have been temporarily closed. These include Qingdao Jiaozhou, Beiping Nancheng, Shandong Weixian, Jiangsu Chenjiagang, Qintong, Danyang, Anhui Chuzhou, Datong, and Wuhe, Hubei Yuejiakou and Shayang, Henan Zhumadian Zhangde and Lingbao, Hebei Shijiazhuang, and fifteen other locations. Those established to meet business needs include the Anhui Hefei Office, the Beiping Xicheng Office (relocated from the Nancheng Office), and the Wuchang Wangshanmen Office. Those reorganized include the Jiangxi Province-managed line, which was moved from Jiujiang to the Desheng Road Office in Nanchang; the Guangrunmen Nanchang Branch, which was changed to the Guangrunmen Office; the former Jiujiang-managed line, which was changed to the Jiujiang Branch; the Liyang Agency, which had good business and was expanded into an office; and the Yichang Branch, which was changed to an office due to changes in the business environment. All of these measures are intended to improve business convenience. Overview of Savings Department Business At the end of this year, the total savings deposit balance was over 31.5 million yuan, of which current savings deposits were over 20.9 million yuan, a decrease from the previous year, and fixed savings deposits were over 10.5 million yuan, an increase from the previous year. This year, to meet the needs of depositors, three types of savings were added: fixed deposit lump sum withdrawal, fixed deposit installment payment, and deposit principal interest payment. At the end of this year, the total loan balance was over 21 million yuan, and the total amount of securities purchased was over 6.6 million yuan. The content of loans and investments complies with the Savings Bank Law. The current public reserve of the department is 600,000 yuan, which also exceeds the capital of 100,000 yuan. Overview of International Department Business Foreign exchange fluctuations were not drastic this year, and the department's operations were more cautious. Various businesses have made progress, and to encourage China's export trade, efforts have been made to promote export documentary bills. Since currency reform, foreign exchange has stabilized, and the department's operating risks have been reduced accordingly. The department's foreign currency reserves are increasing, and the business foundation can be considered solid. Overview of Trust Department Business This year, the department applied to the government to be established as a specialized department, allocating an additional capital of 500,000 yuan. Accounting is independent of the business department. This year, business focused on safekeeping valuables and deeds for customers, acting as an agent for receiving and paying funds, providing guarantees for customers, providing insurance for customers, and managing real estate affairs. Progress is smooth.

Service Overview

This year, the bank adopted a policy of solidifying reserves as its business strategy, and has not been able to actively promote assistance to industry, commerce, and agriculture. However, it continues to provide assistance to stable production enterprises within a safe range, and continues to facilitate the turnover of ordinary people's finances. Assistance to National Industry From January to October this year, currency continued to contract, and the market became increasingly depressed. Various industries struggled to maintain turnover, and many reduced production and cut expenses to survive. Since currency reform, inventory prices have risen, and sales have improved. Various factories have benefited, especially those that use domestic raw materials, such as silk factories, oil factories, and some yarn factories and flour mills. This year, loans to national industries totaled over 33.75 million yuan, a decrease of over 3.3 million yuan from the previous year, due to loan contraction. The content of the loans can be analyzed as follows: Among the loans, the largest decrease compared to the previous year was in loans to yarn factories, reaching over 3 million yuan, followed by dyeing and weaving factories, which decreased by over 400,000 yuan. The rest were similar to the previous year. Collateral accounted for over 90% of the loans, focusing on the pledge of bulk commodities. For large-amount collateral loans, cooperation with other banks was still used to diversify loan risk. Efforts were also continued to promote management and technology. The most gratifying phenomenon this year is that the operating efficiency of various factories has generally increased in the depressed environment. The cost of each bale of cotton yarn in yarn factories is not inferior to that of excellent foreign factories in China. If they can continue to innovate, and at the same time, local security and diplomacy are worry-free, then national industries can be expected to make progress in the future. Assistance to the Rural Economy The bank has been providing rural loans for more than four years. Although the task is arduous, it is difficult to say that the bank has made significant contributions. Fortunately, the staff went deep into the countryside and worked tirelessly to maintain a steady progress in the adverse environment. Although disasters occurred one after another, cotton production was relatively abundant, and agricultural exports were relatively active, and prices were relatively stable. Therefore, rural loans increased compared to the previous year. The total loan amount for the year was over 6.08 million yuan, an increase of over 1.5 million yuan compared to the previous year. The loan area is distributed in Shanghai and Nanjing, and in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Shandong, Shanxi, Guangdong, Henan, Shanxi, Hubei, Hunan, and ten other provinces, in a total of 70 counties. There are over 900 cooperatives and warehouses that have borrowed from the bank, and 200,000 farmers have financial relationships with the bank. The types of loans can be summarized as follows: (A) Production and sales loans: This type of loan is provided to cooperatives and farmers for production or transportation and sales, with crops as collateral. The term is short and greatly benefits the financial turnover of farmers. It has always been the main business of the bank's agricultural loans. This year, a total of over 3.7 million yuan was lent out. The important crops used as collateral are cotton in Shaanxi, Zhejiang, and Jiangsu, silk and tobacco in Shandong, sugarcane in Guangdong, and tea, wheat, and tobacco in Anhui. (B) Credit loans: This type of loan is granted to credit cooperatives for production improvement, and is distributed in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hubei, and Shandong provinces. Each credit cooperative has been thoroughly investigated and deemed to have sound organization and reliable guarantees before loans are granted. This year, credit loans totaling over 460,000 yuan were granted. (C) Warehouse agricultural product pledge loans: This type of pledge loan is undertaken by cooperative warehouses, special warehouses, or directly by the bank. The pledge loan made this year was 1.8 million yuan. (D) Other loans: There is a type of loan called "ox club loans." The so-called ox club is a collective organization for the purpose of preserving draft cattle. Loans are provided for production purposes, with draft cattle as collateral. This was piloted in Jiangning, Jiangpu, and Yicheng this year, with good results. A total of over 110,000 yuan was lent out during the year, and all have been repaid upon maturity. Many of the loans granted this year were jointly granted with other banks, and were handled very smoothly. Since the bank is providing rural relief from the perspective of a commercial bank, its scope cannot be too broad. If it can work together with other banks, it can not only eliminate unnecessary competition, but also achieve greater results. Assistance to Civilian Finance The Jing'an Temple Road branch of the bank has been providing small credit loans for five years, and has been handled with great care. The results have been very good over the years. This year, even in the environment of financial panic, it has still made a considerable contribution. At the end of this year, the loan balance was over 499,000 yuan, similar to the end of the previous year. The number of borrowers was over 6,980, which is double the number of the previous year. The reasons for borrowing and the types of borrowers are similar to those of the previous year. In total, the number of borrowers since the establishment of the program has reached over 15,000, indicating that the service does meet the needs of the general public. What is particularly gratifying is that the amount of bad debt is very small, less than 5/10,000th of the total loan amount. Each loan is not a large amount, and there are reliable guarantors. Loans are only granted after a thorough investigation, which is quite stable and reliable for bank operations. This year, in order to reduce the interest burden on borrowers, the original interest rate of 7.5% per month was reduced to 6% per month. However, for those who overdue on repayments, a late fee of 5 jiao is charged to encourage borrowers to repay on time.

Tung Wah Plays with Nine Men - Loses 1-3 to French Club - Li Ning, Li Yichen, and Zhou Guangzhong Injured - French Club's Performance Mediocre, Victory Not Glorious 135

The Tung Wah and French Club football teams both hold prominent positions in the Western Union Group A League. Yesterday's meeting at the Recreation Ground was crucial for the championship outcome, so both sides acted cautiously and fielded their strongest lineups. Unexpectedly, disaster struck Tung Wah with an unfortunate major sacrifice. Li Mi, Li Yichen, and Zhou Guangzhong were successively injured and left the field. In the end, they fought with only nine men. Their hopes turned into frustration. The five thousand spectators also lost their spirit. Both Li Ning and Li Yichen were injured, one in the wrist and one in the forehead. It is feared that they will not recover in the short term. The match ended in a miserable 1-3 defeat.

Three Generals Injured

In the first five minutes, the battle was unusually fierce. The extremely rapid and brilliant performance earned enthusiastic praise from the audience. Unexpectedly, at this moment, Li Ning lost his footing while saving a ball, fell and injured his wrist severely, and left the field. Tung Wah felt the pain of losing a main player, but continued to attack. The momentum was still strong. But after half an hour, Li Yichen (the original inside defender) headed the ball. At the same time, French Club center forward Robertsdorf rushed up and kicked the ball with his foot, hitting Li's forehead and brow. Tung Wah lost these two main players and has since failed. In the tenth minute of the second half, Zhou Guangzhong was also injured in the foot and left the field. From then on, it became a one-sided situation.

Lucky Victory

The French Club had won eight games in a row, but yesterday's performance was mediocre. In the face of Tung Wah's defeat, there was no special development. The talent was very good, but there were many shortcomings in the connection. The French Club was disturbed by Tung Wah's generals, revealing an uneasy look. The forward was also scattered and disorganized. The three goals were not scored with a clean kick. It only shows a lucky victory.

A Glimpse of the Situation

After Li Ning was injured, Mai Youliang scored a goal for Tung Wah, and the situation was extremely exciting. Tung Wah did not reduce its fighting power due to Li Ning's injury. Tung Wah occupied the advantage for 20 minutes before being cleverly passed by French Club right winger Walter, and Robertsdorf scored a diagonal shot, creating a tie. After that, Li Yichen was injured, and Tung Wah continued to struggle. The French Club was still helpless. Until the 40th minute, Jaimie Walter scored another goal, and the first half ended 2-1. Afterwards, Tung Wah fought like a trapped beast. Everyone doubled their efforts and ran the entire field, shouldering the double responsibility of offense and defense. After all, the strength was weak, and the response was not timely. The French Club center forward scored another goal. The French Club showed a scattered and weak posture everywhere. From then on, they could no longer increase the number of goals. The lineups of both sides are as follows:

Educational News: The Ministry of Education Promulgates Revised Registration Rules and Work Outline for Middle School Training Directors and Civics Teachers

The Ministry of Education issued a circular on the 4th to the Education Bureaus of various provinces and cities, stating: "The Central Executive Committee's Department of Mass Training's Document No. 1128, dated March 6, 1936, states, 'Upon review, there are many places in the Review Regulations for the Qualifications of Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools and the Review Regulations for the Qualifications of Training Directors in Secondary Schools, which were passed by the 86th Standing Committee Meeting of the previous four Central Executive Committees on August 31, 1933, that should be revised. Moreover, having two sets of regulations promulgated for the same type of event should be merged into one to demonstrate order. Furthermore, the Organizational Regulations for the Review Committee for the Qualifications of Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools, which were also passed on the same day, are flawed in both name and content and should be revised separately. The Regulations for the Review of the Qualifications of Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools and the Revised Organizational Regulations for the Review Committee for the Qualifications of Training Directors and Civics Teachers have been drafted and submitted to the Sixth Standing Committee Meeting of the Central Executive Committee for approval, and the previously promulgated Review Regulations for the Qualifications of Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools and Review Regulations for the Qualifications of Training Directors have been abolished. Now, the Registration Rules for Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools and the Work Outline for Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools, which are related to the above regulations, have been revised and supplemented, and a new Method for Evaluating the Work Performance of Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools has been drafted to ensure effective evaluation and promote the advancement of Party ideology education. In addition to being implemented, relevant documents are enclosed for your review and compliance.' In addition to the Regulations for the Review of the Qualifications of Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools and the Revised Organizational Regulations for the Review Committee for the Qualifications of Training Directors and Civics Teachers, which have been forwarded to the Ministry of Education by the Executive Yuan and have been circulated for compliance, copies of the Revised Registration Rules for Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools, the Revised Work Outline for Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools, and the Method for Evaluating the Work Performance of Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools are enclosed for your compliance and transmission to your subordinates for uniform compliance. This order includes one copy of the Revised Registration Rules for Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools, one copy of the Revised Work Outline for Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools, and three copies of the Method for Evaluating the Work Performance of Training Directors and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools."

Revised Registration Rules for Middle School Training Directors and Civics Teachers 146

(Promulgated and implemented by the Central Guidance Committee for Mass Movement on April 9, 1934; revised by the Department of Mass Training of the Fifth Central Executive Committee on March 1, 1936) Article 1: These rules are formulated by the Central Department of Mass Training (hereinafter referred to as "the Department") to facilitate the service of training directors and civics teachers in secondary schools across the country and to make it easier for the qualification review committees of training directors and civics teachers in various provinces and cities to guide and evaluate. Article 2: All training directors and civics teachers in secondary schools who have passed the review must register with the Department in accordance with these rules. Article 3: When registering, the provincial or municipal review committee that originally issued the qualification certificate must be responsible for forwarding the request for registration; individuals may not apply directly. Article 4: When registering, the name, age, place of origin, gender, party membership status, and qualification certificate number of the qualified personnel must be compiled into a form, along with two recent three-inch half-length photos, and submitted to the Department for processing. Article 5: After registration, the Department will issue a registration certificate, the format of which will be determined separately. Article 6: Those who hold a registration certificate must, when changing their place of service, report to the review committee at the place of arrival with the registration certificate for record, and must also report to the review committee at the original location for record. Article 7: The reporting and filing procedures in the preceding article must be completed within one month after starting work. Those who fail to comply within the time limit will be investigated by the local review committee, and a deadline will be set for reporting. If the delay continues, the Department may be requested to impose a penalty. Article 8: The review committees of each province and city shall, within one month after the start of each semester, compile a statistical table of the training directors and civics teachers in secondary schools within their respective provinces and cities and submit it to the Department for record. Article 9: These rules may be amended by the Department if there are any omissions. Article 10: These rules shall be promulgated and implemented by the Department. (To be continued)

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (Part 2) (〇)(一) 156

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"Hush! Hush!" cried the children, and then a hush fell, because the boy's shy manner and earnest eyes made everyone want to listen quietly.

The Bhaers thought he was going to play a familiar tune, but to their surprise, they heard a new and lovely tune, played very gently and tenderly. They could hardly believe it was Ned playing. It was a tune without words but could touch people's hearts, singing of all the hopes and joys of mankind, giving comfort and joy to those who heard this pure music. Aunt Meg leaned on Little Bridge's shoulder, Grandma wiped her tears, and Mrs. Jo looked up at Mr. Bhaer and said softly in words too moved to speak,

"That's your score."

Mr. Bhaer bowed his head and replied, "I have asked this boy of yours to perform well for your glory, and to express his gratitude to you in his own way."

Economic Supplement

The Core of Reducing Interest Rates 157

— Wei Youpei

Currently, the issue of low interest rates is being jointly studied by the government and commercial organizations. Both the banking and financial industries have separately formed subcommittees to discuss ways to reduce interest rates. What has been the result? All we hear about are records of actions, but we never see any concrete implementation measures. The reason for this hesitant research is not simply due to the "great importance of the matter," but is actually due to practical difficulties.

A low interest rate era in general economic terms signifies two things: one is that it indicates that the economy is in a process of decline, and the other is that it indicates the early stages of economic recovery. It can also be said that low interest rates are a kind of stepping stone from an era of economic decline to an era of economic recovery. The level of interest rates is nothing more than the general situation of supply and demand. Therefore, low interest rates indicate that the need for capital is decreasing at that time, and all economic activities are contracting. From 1860 to the outbreak of the Great War, the highest unemployment rates for British workers were in 1879, 1886, and 1909, with unemployment percentages of 11%, 10%, and 8%, respectively. The Bank of England's rediscount rates during these years averaged 2.5% in 1879, 3% in 1886, and 3.25% in 1909. This example can prove that low interest rates and increased unemployment rates are in an inverse proportion.

However, this indication of low interest rates is significantly different from the current economic situation in China. The former explains that low interest rates move along with the socio-economic state, while the latter wants to use this path to achieve the goal of economic recovery.

According to the statistics of the Iron Industry Monthly, the average interest rates in Shanghai during the panic over the past six years are as follows: 7 fen per thousand yuan daily interest in the 19th year, 1 jiao 3 fen in the 20th year, 8 fen in the 21st year, 6 fen in the 22nd year, 6 fen in the 23rd year, and 1 jiao 4 fen in the 24th year. The year with the highest interest rate was also the year with the most profound panic. This fact is the exact opposite of the example given above. The low interest rates in the UK indicate economic decline, while in our country, it is the opposite. The reason is that the UK is a suzerain state, their financial organization is sound, and various industries have many colonies as their outlet. Therefore, what they feel in economic decline is overproduction and stagnant capital. Our country is a semi-colonial economic country, with unsound industrial and financial organizations, and general capital is not necessarily used for production. Therefore, the most difficult thing felt during a panic is credit contraction. In the UK during that period, factories were resting, and there was no need for capital operation, so interest rates were low. In our country during this period, due to credit contraction, industrial and commercial operators needed capital assistance but found it difficult to achieve their goals, so interest rates rose. Therefore, in terms of this issue, if we reduce interest rates in our country to seek economic recovery, this principle is correct.

The capital of production enterprises mostly relies on the use of loans. The level of loan interest rates is also the level of production costs. Therefore, a low interest rate policy is sufficient to reduce production costs and promote the progress of production enterprises.

The reason why the market interest rate in our country is so high is due to the abnormal development of cities and the fact that funds are not created through proper use. Since the extreme expansion of urban finance, funds have been accumulated without a way out, so most of them tend to take the path of speculation. The easiest examples to cite are real estate, public bonds, bid money, and goods. The generous profits of this kind of speculation are all higher than those of general industry and commerce, which is a manifestation of the expansion of urban finance. That is, the increase in the number of banks in recent years, and the interest obtained from regular industrial and commercial lending, is naturally not as high as that of speculation, so they all abandon this and take that. At the same time, in order to increase their profits, banks have to use high interest rates to absorb deposits as their speculative capital. The Shanghai market is declining every year, the national economy is declining every year, and the profits of the banking industry have always stood in an invincible position. With the changes of the times and the gradual contraction of credit, urban real estate prices have fallen with the economic downturn, and a large number of speculators have felt the pain of credit freeze. Due to the deepening of credit, there have also been bank runs, which have shaken the foundation of banks. Their only way out is still to use high interest rate methods to absorb deposits to strengthen their foundation. Real estate has fallen, but other speculative policies are still emerging endlessly. Why should banks "not follow this path"? It is really difficult for industrialists and merchants to hope for a turnover of funds.

And what about the rural areas? Due to the outflow of funds, the drop in the price of agricultural products, and the frequent occurrence of natural and man-made disasters, there is a great lack of payment chips. Funds have been concentrated in cities, and it is difficult for the drop in the price of agricultural products and poor harvests to bring back funds. Where do farmers get funds in this difficult situation? According to the survey of the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute, the largest percentage of farmers' loan sources is rich farmers, followed by merchants and landlords, and cooperatives account for only 1%. Since there are no formal financial institutions, it is of course an ideal to hope for fair interest rates. Farmers who ask for loans can only struggle under usury.

Usury is a fact in our country, and it is also a fact that it harms industry and agriculture. Then, of course, it cannot be said that it is unreasonable to demand low interest rates, but there are still many practical problems.

In his article "From Bank Interest Rates to Interest Rate Reduction" published in this newspaper, Mr. Sheng Kezhong stated his views on reducing interest rates and proposed a hypothetical highest and lowest standard interest rate, which is 6% for both ordinary and savings one-year deposits, and 5% to 7% monthly interest for loans. Mr. Sheng believes that the source of industrial and commercial loans is banks, and the interest rate on deposits is actually the cost of the bank's loan interest rate, so we should first seek a reduction in deposit interest. According to the interest rates he set, compared with advanced countries, it is obviously still much higher.

Now, from the bank's point of view, there are many difficulties in reducing interest rates. The most obvious is that there are many high-interest investments ahead, and there is no need to find a way out for loans, which cannot be corrected. Taking public bonds as an example, since the government unified them, the interest rate has been reduced somewhat, but no matter what, it is always above 8%, and its stability is also above that of general investments.

Bank capital is also a kind of cost, and the interest rate of this cost is the dividend. The usual dividend interest rate is 6% to 8%. If you want to reduce interest rates, in addition to reducing the interest on deposits, you must also consider the dividend. Dividends can certainly be reduced, but bank stocks, which originally did not occupy any position in commercial securities, may be devalued as a result.

The escape of capital is also a matter of concern. Have we not seen foreign banks revise their deposit news? The announcement in the newspaper stated that the interest rate was reduced, but in fact, not only was the interest rate not reduced, but it was still increased. Haven't we heard of foreign banks refusing to accept deposits? Haven't we heard of foreign banks not giving interest on deposits and giving them "free deposits"? The current revision of interest rates has actually become an increase. This is a matter that should be paid attention to in the promotion of low interest rates. Although it is said that the Chinese people have made great progress in common sense recently, and they no longer trust foreign banks as much as before, after the currency reform, it is common to see the general bourgeoisie purchasing and storing foreign currency, purchasing and storing foreign goods, and hoarding gold bars. Then, once the interest rate is reduced, there is not much difference between Chinese banks and foreign banks for many depositors. Why not abandon this and take that?

The social situation in China is different from that in other countries. The form of feudal society has not been completely abandoned, so it is not surprising that the high interest rate in the folk is as high as 100% in poor and remote areas. Although the reduction of interest rates can be uniformly reduced in urban banks, it is impossible to prevent usury in the folk. In fact, this kind of folk usury has a greater impact on the national economy than that of urban usury. It is still possible to obtain funds by means of usury in cities, but in rural areas, even if they are willing to bear high interest rates, they still have the pain of not being able to obtain them!

The pain suffered by the industrial circles in our country is actually the problem of not being able to obtain funds, not the problem of high or low interest rates! It is a fact that the industrial circles need capital assistance, and it would be even better if they could borrow at low interest rates. But now, in a frozen situation, suppose that the industrial circles still cannot get the convenience of using funds under low interest rates, what kind of measures will be adopted? Therefore, the biggest pain suffered by the industrial circles in our country at present is how to fundamentally solve the problem of credit freeze, not the problem of mere interest rates.

The banking industry is unwilling to engage in regular investment and does not provide funds to industry and commerce because of the generous profits of speculative business or semi-speculative trading. Therefore, to make investment go to the regular road, it is necessary to first strictly crack down on speculation and reduce debt interest. As for the way out for the industrial circles, it lies in expanding the scope of securities and opening up commercial securities, creating a long-term capital turnover market for industry and commerce. There is no need to rely solely on the banks.

The biggest reason for the formation of folk usury is that our country's financial institutions pay too much attention to the urban international commodity market and neglect the rural areas. Therefore, the universal establishment of rural financial institutions is also an indispensable thing. It is the responsibility of everyone to communicate the finance of the city and the village.

In short, the implementation of low interest rates is beneficial to the whole country, but from the standpoint of today's economic situation, if we say that interest rate reduction is the only way out for industry and commerce, and it is the realization of economic recovery, it is too simple.

After this article was written, I saw the Bank Association's subcommittee issue two opinions on interest rate reduction: (1) Request the government to reduce the interest rate on public bonds, and (2) Request the central bank to reveal low interest rates. (Shen Bao, February 27) Although this opinion did not explicitly state that low interest rates are not feasible, it does indicate the necessary conditions for low interest rates. We believe that low interest rates are an indication of the state of capital supply. If we want to obtain capital easing from low interest rates, under today's Chinese financial market, it is not only a practical difficulty, but also putting the cart before the horse. —February 27—.

On Capital Accumulation and Interest Rate Levels 158

— Yu Xun

It is generally recognized that the excessive cost of capital is the core of the problem preventing the development of industry in our country. Therefore, creating a cheap capital market has become the goal of recent public and private efforts. It is generally believed that the implementation of a low interest rate policy should start with reducing the government's public debt interest. Since the government announced the method of unifying public debt, the interest rate is still 6%, and it has not been reduced in any way compared to before. It is generally argued that this is because the government's policy is not thorough enough. But we believe that the first issue that should be studied here is whether it is possible to artificially reduce interest rates?

The level of interest rates in a society is determined by various objective environments. However, broadly speaking, it mainly depends on two factors: supply and demand. In societies with abundant capital accumulation, the supply of capital is sufficient, and the elasticity is very large, so the level of interest rates is generally low, and seasonal changes are relatively insignificant. On the other hand, in economically backward countries with weak capital accumulation, the supply of capital is not very sufficient, and there is a lack of elastic flexibility, so the level of interest rates is generally high, and seasonal changes are very significant. From the demand side, in times of prosperity, prices rise, industry is active, and industrialists rise up to engage in activities, and the level of interest rates must be raised. In certain seasons, certain businesses are particularly active, which can also push up the level of interest rates, which is the so-called financial season. For example, if an investment in a certain local business is particularly profitable, such as real estate a few years ago, so that the activities of social capital tend to one path, the result can also raise the level of interest rates. The interest rates in a society are generally determined by the relationship between supply and demand. If the relationship between supply and demand does not change, and the interest rate is reduced by artificial methods, what will be the result? Those who own capital are unwilling to invest it, or even invest it in other places, and the supply of capital becomes increasingly reduced. The result will inevitably lead to a long-term economic decline, and we will never be able to keep up with others. Therefore, unnatural reduction of interest rates is an unhealthy means in economics.

Moreover, based on historical experience, artificially suppressing interest rates often fails to achieve the goal and becomes an ineffective effort. For example, if we reduce the public debt interest rate to 3%, the market price of public debt may fall to thirty-one or two yuan, but the result is still about one fen. If we raise the public debt interest rate to 8%, the market price of public debt may be as high as eighty-four or five yuan, but the result is still about one fen interest. Therefore, before other environments have changed, the market price of public debt will rise and fall on its own to adapt to the interest rate and meet a certain standard interest rate. Simply raising or lowering the public debt interest rate will ultimately have no effect.

Based on the facts of the past and present, "one fen" seems to be the most common interest rate in the public debt market in our country, and 60 to 70 yuan will probably become the most common market price for public debt in our country. One fen interest may be a more natural interest rate in our country's capital market. Our country's capital accumulation is still in its infancy, and it is inevitable that capital will be more expensive. Because of this, we can encourage general capital accumulation, so that our capital accumulation can stand at the same level as other countries. Therefore, as long as our country's interest rate is not too different from that of other countries, it is harmless to be slightly higher, and it is also natural.

One fen interest is still too heavy from the standpoint of industry and commerce. For example, the material of a piece of foreign clothing is exactly the same as ours, but the interest cost they bear is only two jiao, while ours is more than one yuan. In this way, our products are obviously at a disadvantage in the market. Therefore, it is necessary to gradually suppress domestic interest rates to reach the international interest rate level. The second question we want to discuss is how can we achieve this goal?

Since the level of interest rates generally depends on the supply and demand of capital, we must design from these two aspects if we want to gradually reduce the level of interest rates in our country. If we can increase the supply of capital on the one hand and conserve the use of capital on the other, our goal can be gradually achieved. Therefore, under the premise of a low interest rate policy, we want to propose two points: one is to encourage capital accumulation, and the other is to control the use of capital.

Without accumulation, there is no capital. Capital comes from accumulation. A portion of what people get from production is not used for consumption, but is invested in production enterprises, so that it can be produced again. This is capital. Therefore, the meaning of capital is the re-production of production income. In economically developed societies, people's production efficiency is very high. There is more surplus in life, so the capital accumulation efficiency is also greater, the supply of capital is naturally more abundant, and the level of interest rates is also lower. On the other hand, in economically backward societies, people's productivity is very low, and what they earn in a day is not enough to support themselves. Naturally, there is no surplus for accumulation, and the level of interest rates cannot but be higher. Therefore, the interest rate problem is fundamentally a capital accumulation problem. And the biggest difficulty facing our country at present is the lack of production capital. The rise in interest rates is the result of a lack of production capital, not the cause. The problem we are facing at present is how to encourage capital accumulation. After this problem is solved, other problems will be solved accordingly. A slightly higher interest rate level is not a problem, and it is a way to encourage people's capital accumulation.

Secondly, controlling the use of capital is also a hand that must be adopted under the premise of a low interest rate policy. Capital is the basis of economic activity, and it can also be said to be the foothold for human survival. If the accumulated capital is not used for production enterprises, then not only will interest rates rise, but also human survival will become impossible. Therefore, how to control the use of capital has become a policy that must be adopted. However, because of the different eras, the degree of adoption is slightly different. The ancient people's interest in fishing and salt, and the development of mountain forests, are nothing more than a kind of control strategy for capital activities. For example, the so-called rationalization of industry a few years ago was nothing more than controlling the activities of capital to make the most efficient production. As for the recently popular controlled economy, analyzing the content is nothing more than strictly managing the direction of capital movement to meet the needs of the society and the country. In economically backward countries with weak capital, controlling the use of capital is a policy that must be adopted. If the activities of capital are allowed to be anarchic, then production becomes anarchic production, and the result is very dangerous. Non-productive businesses that divert the use of capital should be stopped. For example, real estate solidifies hundreds of millions of capital, but it has no direct production effect. This kind of business should be stopped from developing. Unhealthy industries often waste capital unnecessarily. Taoist industries should be urged to improve, so that capital can exert its productive effect. Hopeless industries freeze and delay the use of useful capital. These industries should be eliminated to avoid wasting useful capital in hopeless ways. For example, it should be forbidden to borrow debts for non-production purposes, and to rob production capital, so as to avoid using production capital for non-production purposes, or even for destruction of production expenditures. All capital should be used for production purposes, and all can be produced most efficiently. This is the policy we should adopt in the future. Only in this way can the ability of capital accumulation be increased, and the large-scale accumulation of capital is possible. Only after sufficient capital accumulation can the social interest rate level naturally decrease.

If the accumulation of capital in society does not increase, but only artificially lowers interest rates, it is abandoning the fundamental and pursuing the superficial, and it is unnatural. It is not only ineffective, but also harmful. We believe that the crux of the current industrial problem in our country is not that the interest rate level is too high, but that the accumulated capital is not enough to be applied, and that only some of the capital is wasted in non-production ways. The current way to rescue is to encourage capital accumulation and control the use of capital. It is useless to talk empty words about reducing interest rates without this plan.

Shanghai Real Estate in 1935 159

— Xu Jin

In 1933, Shanghai's real estate market, due to the influx of urban speculative capital and general speculative fervor, showed signs of gradual prosperity. The annual real estate transaction volume reached 43,136,000 yuan. Although this was a decrease of over 130 million yuan compared to the golden age before the "January 28th Incident" (i.e., 1931), it was an increase of over 18 million yuan compared to 1932. Undoubtedly, Shanghai's real estate market at that time did have a period of vigorous growth.

Unfortunately, however, by 1934, this glimmer of hope was extinguished. This is because real estate, after all, needs people to live in it to generate rent. This means that it is ultimately subject to the ups and downs of industry and commerce. And China's economy in 1934 was plagued by various ills, and Shanghai was no exception. The United States' silver purchase policy, which became popular in 1934 (especially in the second half of the year), made Shanghai, already suffering from financial inflation, feel the threat of tight credit and scarcity of funds. As a result, land prices plummeted and even became lifeless assets that no one cared about. Previously, silver firms that had been obsessed with "title deeds" suffered greatly at this time, and they all declared bankruptcy due to the inability to circulate huge amounts of real estate mortgages. As a result, the real estate relief problem became extremely serious!

In the spring of 1935, Shanghai real estate merchants, in order to extricate themselves from their predicament, proposed issuing 500 million yuan of real estate securities, using real estate as collateral, so that dead real estate could be revived and circulated. However, this resulted in failure. In August, they planned to establish a real estate exchange, hoping to revive real estate through auction floors, but this also resulted in failure! This is not surprising. When afflicted with a terminal illness, even Bian Que (a legendary doctor) could not bring one back to life! Sir Victor Sassoon, the British gentleman and real estate magnate of Shanghai, in order to fill the gaps in his coffers, also advocated the issuance of pound notes last spring to resist the encroachment of the silver policy and allow land prices to continue to rise. As a result, due to "unripe timing," it temporarily vanished like a bubble. However, Sir Sassoon's opinion was ultimately much stronger than that of Chinese real estate developers. It also had the air of an international currency war, and the British Royal Family would not take it lightly. Therefore, Ross came to China, and the pound note plan was largely realized through the new monetary system!

Of course, we are not saying that the new legal tender and pound notes are the same thing, but we are also unwilling to blindly deny the blood relationship between them. At the same time, we are not saying that Ross's instigation of the new monetary policy in China was entirely in response to Sir Sassoon's demands. We only believe that the policy also very effectively served Sir Sassoon's real estate! Because after the birth of the new legal tender, the Ministry of Finance could worry less about the suffering of depleted silver reserves and enjoy more freedom to issue banknotes. Not only could the fiscal figures be temporarily balanced, but general credit could also be eased. Wouldn't this allow real estate to take the opportunity to revive? Let's listen to the explanations of Arthur and Sopher! They wrote with a smile in the Shanghai Times:

"Regardless of whether the Chinese government will be able to support its new monetary policy in the future, assuming other conditions remain unchanged, the real estate market will develop upwards. Because if the new legal tender is successful, then abundant new legal tender and flexible credit will flow into the real estate sector to find profitable outlets. If the new legal tender fails, then real estate can also be revitalized through speculative transactions. Therefore, the timing for investing in real estate is indeed ripe!"

According to the facts, this is indeed the case. Before October, real estate transactions were very quiet. In June, the Puyi Real Estate Company even went bankrupt due to the decline in real estate. However, after November, the situation was very different. The transaction volume of real estate increased sharply, as detailed in the table below:

Shanghai Real Estate Transaction Volume Table for 1935 (Unit: Yuan)

From the previous table, we can immediately see that almost half of the annual transaction volume of over 14 million yuan belonged to the months of November and December. Therefore, looking at the whole year, although the transaction volume only increased by over 2 million yuan compared to 1934, and does not indicate any improvement in the real estate industry, from the perspective of the last two months, it does show significant vitality.

The sudden increase in real estate transaction volume in November and December is also related to the surge in remittances from overseas Chinese, but the latter is itself caused by the new legal tender. This is because the exchange rate of the new legal tender against foreign currencies was consistently lower than before, which increased the value of remittances from overseas Chinese when converted. According to the recent response from Li Daonan, Chairman of the Hong Kong Chinese Banks Association, to Sir Ross, the remittances from overseas Chinese in 1935 increased by 40% compared to the previous year (see the Hong Kong Industrial and Commercial Daily on February 19th). And due to the increasing decline of the domestic economy, most of these remittances were used to purchase real estate.

The promulgation of the new monetary policy, according to the Ministry of Finance's announcement at the time, was intended to revive industry and commerce. We will not discuss for the time being what kind of achievements have been made in this regard, but Shanghai's real estate industry has indeed been quite "revived." Sassoon, Hardoon, and general real estate owners will be deeply grateful, but from the perspective of the future of the national economy, this is extremely regrettable! It should be understood that after the rise of real estate, social funds have no longer paid attention to low-profit or even precarious industry and commerce!

There are two additional reasons why the real estate industry showed signs of a turnaround last year that must also be pointed out. The first is that the Shanghai Silver Industry Association and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce jointly launched a revision of the Mortgage Law, that is, if a real estate mortgage is not paid off upon maturity, the mortgagee can automatically sell it without having to first apply to the court for approval as in the past. The second is that the Ministry of Finance repeatedly ordered the China Construction Bank to establish a real estate mortgage bank to strengthen and expand the scope of real estate mortgages. Although these two things are still in progress, the force stimulating real estate to become active has already occurred. These two things are clearly instigated by silver firms and general real estate merchants. There is nothing wrong with this in itself, but they have forgotten the most fundamental problem and are abandoning the root to pursue the branch, which is really unforgivable.

In 1935, Shanghai's real estate market enjoyed considerable vitality thanks to the new monetary policy, but the entire national economy was still sinking in panic. This is a stark contrast that we should not forget! What right do we have to laugh with Sassoon! —Night of March 1, 1936

Securities The Bond Market of China and Europe Amidst Many Accidents Hovers and酝酿… Transactions are Very Quiet 161

Last week, from March 9th to 14th, the public bond market of the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange suddenly encountered two major accidents at home and abroad. Market prices were precarious. Although there were several pullbacks, the overall trend was weak. Externally, the situation in Europe became increasingly tense. The pent-up resentment of many years erupted at once, which was more violent than any previous event. Therefore, it is impossible to temporarily declare stability at this moment. The issue of security concerning all countries in the world is extremely important. The situation in Germany and France is closely watched by the whole world. All industries related to the whole world are also shaken by it. Internally, the North China problem is still complex, and suddenly there are rumors of the Min Incident. Public bonds are in the midst of these two major crises. Without the establishment of an equalization committee, there would have been endless waves and it would be difficult to have the current situation of hovering,酝酿 and quiet transactions. The future situation, due to the increase in public bond chips, if the environment evolves slightly, then the changes will inevitably follow suit. For the time being, it is really not optimistic. Looking back on last week, on Monday, the German troops entered the demilitarized zone of the Rhine River, and the declaration of Hitler shocked the public bond market of the world. Our country's public bonds were no exception. The North Gang and No. 47 and others were sold in large quantities, and market prices fell back by 67 cents. On Tuesday, people were still uneasy. Tidbits 166

— (Xiao Bai)

Fear is the greatest enemy of mankind. All so-called anxiety, worry, timidity, and panic are really manifestations of fear. It deprives people of happiness and weakens their abilities. It will make people increasingly cowardly and useless, and make them fail.

The evolution of society and the efforts of mankind, at present, in the progress of each of our undertakings, there is really no need for fear and procrastination. We must know that the only way to obtain a way out and seek light is to catch up, actively prepare and enrich ourselves, do not hesitate, do not wait and see, and exert the greatest strength.

So we can say: "Procrastination is the culprit of bad things, and fear is the destroyer of all human facts." Every minute of procrastination really makes things more difficult, and every minute of fear makes people lose a greater possibility of realization.

"To do, do it immediately!" I would like everyone to embrace this motto of successful people.

Wu the Coppersmith 167

— Jia Su

Wu the coppersmith, a native of Jiangxi. In his youth, he was open-minded and unrestrained, flaunted his ambition to the world, and did not care about fame and fortune. He was strong and often wrestled with the children in his village, all of whom were defeated by him. Next to his house were two stone dumbbells. He lifted them with both arms, and the two dumbbells rose up without any sign of weakness. His neighbor was the residence of a certain magistrate, whose power and influence were dazzling and unparalleled. Whenever he went out, he would raise flags and umbrellas, and his servants would be like clouds. When Wu saw this, he cursed: "Why do you flaunt yourself like this! You are arrogant because of your official position. What is an official? An official is a servant of the people. Even the emperor cannot go beyond this. My ambition is not to be an official." His peers laughed at him, calling him a madman. Before long, the magistrate injured someone with his sedan chair. The wife of the injured person sought compensation, but he refused and flogged her, driving her away. Wu raised his arms and shouted: "The person who injured someone should be punished. If you are a magistrate, can you violate the law! I should kill you!" His parents had always disapproved of him, seeing him as a domineering little boy who was incorrigible, and they secretly intended to drive him away. The next day, the magistrate's office heard of an assassin, and Wu disappeared without a trace. Wu and the former Governor Zhang Xun of the capital were sworn brothers. When Xun controlled the Huai River with his army, those who sold titles swarmed around him like ants, and some tried to persuade him to advance. Wu was angry and said: "Wealth and honor are not my wish. Even though Xun is my sworn brother, since he is so prominent, how can I bend my knees and fawn on him because of poverty and lowliness?" When Wu moved to Zhenjiang, he became a coppersmith, and was therefore called Wu the coppersmith. And people also called him Wu the coppersmith, and forgot his name. Wu was happy and enjoyed it, and was not humiliated in his heart. When Xun passed through Zhenjiang, he visited his hut and wanted to entrust him with an official position, but Wu resolutely refused, saying: "I did not want to be an official when I was young. An official is a servant of the people, and it is only to suffer oneself. If one cares about the people, then one is too tired. If one does not care about the people, then one's heart is guilty and restless. Why not wander in the market and live in seclusion?" Wu had a rough understanding of writing and could also write simple letters. His speech was bold and healthy. His hut was no more than dozens of steps away from my house, but I only recently learned about him. Now he is still working as a coppersmith, which is his old ambition.

Inn 168

— Zhu Ying

I went to the interior for some trivial matters. Although the journey was not far, there were no trains or cars on that road. Although there were boats, they traveled at an unexpectedly slow pace. Therefore, even using the only fast means of transportation, the eighteenth-century-style wheelbarrow, I could not arrive that day.

In the weather of February, at about five o'clock, the sun had already hidden below the horizon. Following the advice of my only travel companion, the wheelbarrow driver, to avoid encountering thugs on the way, I stayed at an inn recommended by the driver.

According to the driver, this inn was the only inn on this road where "officials and merchants" stayed. But this inn, rather than being called an inn, was better described as a farmhouse. There was no signboard, just a faded red paper strip stuck on the door, with the barely recognizable four characters "Lishang Inn" written on it. The house was a row of three rooms with a thatched roof and mud walls. The middle room was the hall, which, in addition to a broken wooden table and broken long benches, also had a loom. The owner's bedroom was at the head, and the front of the lower room was the inn, and the back was the kitchen.

Spring Arrives 169

—

The landlady was just under forty years old, and she also wore rouge and powder on her face. Seeing that a lodger had arrived, she busily swept away the chicken droppings and garbage in the client area, and was busy preparing dinner. The ready-made dishes were salted fish and egg soup. The boss never spoke. When he saw that I was about to finish eating, he put on his shoes and went out. As he was leaving, the driver greeted him, "Boss, going to make a fortune?" The boss didn't say anything. The landlady muttered, "Damn it, one day he'll lose his wife to someone."

At eight o'clock, I had just gotten into bed, and the landlady brought in a pot of tea, saying with a smile, "The guest is sleeping so early, is it because you feel lonely?" I quickly said, "No, it's just that I've been traveling all day and I'm tired." Then, the landlady and the driver were talking and laughing outside. I lay there with my eyes open until ten o'clock, coughed, and the landlady came in again, asking me what was wrong. I pretended to snore and ignored her. After eleven o'clock, the fire outside went out, and I finally felt relieved to close my eyes.

The next morning, I was woken up by the crowing of chickens. I hurriedly washed my face, settled the bill, didn't have breakfast, and urged the driver to set off. As the driver lifted the handlebars of the wheelbarrow, I vaguely heard the landlady, standing at the door, sighing deeply.

Little Western Paradise 170

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 24: Profiting Matters More Than Beauty, a Clumsy Man Gives Up His Love; High Aspirations and Healthy Feet, a Strong Man Goes into the Wilderness

Shi Lian smiled: "This is not to discuss any problems, nor is it to ask Mr. Cheng for any help. This is just that we have a little intention to contribute to your husband. Whether your husband listens or not is just a word, and there is no other trouble." Zhiqian was even more confused. In a good mood, why would they contribute any opinions? He smiled and nodded twice, saying: "Your husband is too polite. How can I bear the word 'contribute'?" Li Shi Lian pondered for a while, then smiled: "It's not that there are any opinions to contribute to Mr. Cheng, but that there is a little intention to contribute to Brother Wang Beihai." Hearing this, Zhiqian couldn't help but feel a move in his heart, so he said: "What is that thing? He is just a poor student and doesn't talk much about socializing." Li Shi Lian smiled: "Does Mr. Cheng not know about this matter? To tell you the truth, it's Mr. Jia Duocai, who is the most lively in Little Western Paradise these two days. He wants to buy a large piece of land." Zhiqian hurriedly smiled: "I understand, this piece of land, Beihai is one of the representatives of the seller. Mr. Jia is asking him to reduce the price, right?" Shi Lian saw a cigarette on the table, took one and smoked it. After taking two puffs, he used three fingers to flick the ashes to the side twice, first smiled, then raised his right heel, pressed his toes on the ground, and bounced himself up for a while. Only then did he smile: "Mr. Jia, because of that Miss Zhu, has been so busy these days that he can hardly stand in Little Western Paradise. He has his own legitimate business, and cannot delay the big event for a joke. Therefore, he has quietly moved out at noon today. He wrote a note and handed it to me, stating that the marriage of men and women will not be related to each other in the future." As he spoke, he groped in his pocket for a while, took out a folded piece of paper, and handed it to Zhiqian with both hands to show him. He shook his hands, leaned back, and said: "Matters related to men and women, it is inconvenient for others to participate in this kind of secret." Li Shi Lian blushed and had to put the manuscript back into his pocket. But at this moment, Zhiqian recalled the meaning, so he smiled: "Mr. Wang will probably come to me soon. If Mr. Li is willing to wait here, I can introduce Beihai to talk to you." (415)

Spring Flowers Mocking People 171

— Manzi

In the late Ming Dynasty, Xu 　Zhi wrote to Du Gengshao, saying, "Life is but thirty-six thousand days, and spring only accounts for nine thousand. We, toiling souls, have already spent half of it. The east wind mocks us year after year." This year is even more prone to procrastination. The weather is so cold that there is not a hint of spring. Even the desire for timely enjoyment is held back.

The day before yesterday, I went to see a preview of "Spring Flowers" at the invitation of a friend. Firstly, the hot water heaters blocked the cold air outside the theater; secondly, the languid singing was full of the air of spring, and one almost forgot the "spring of winter."

However, this kind of spring atmosphere cannot last forever. After being battered by storms several times, by the time the music ended and the audience dispersed, a bleak and desolate feeling akin to autumn had descended, especially as the songs of "Spring Flowers" were sung in such different contexts and revealed themselves in the differences, giving me a profound sense of reflection. When I came out of the theater, the cold night air tightened its grip, and seeing the dim expressions on the faces of the people in the yard, I almost burst into tears.

Therefore, I feel that we must grasp the fleeting moment of youth with all our might. We must not be like Jinniang, unconscious and only loving vanity, blown to the west by the east wind and to the east by the west wind, ultimately becoming mud-stained catkins. It is a true waste and squandering of youth.

But then again, Jinniang's life has always been dominated by her environment, unable to control herself. How countless are the pitiable creatures in this world like Jinniang! If the women watching "Spring Flowers" can truly shed tears of sympathy, then the men should also awaken a little and not be like Sun Shanwu and his ilk, taking pleasure in toying with women. One must know that harming others harms oneself. The law of cause and effect may still exist today, or perhaps it is even sanctioned by science?

Spring flowers bloom and fade so easily, how should we cherish and care for them? "Of the ninety days of spring, half have already passed. Do not let the east wind laugh at us!"

Profiles

Epitaph of Sun Chuanfang 172

— Written by Zhang Binglin of Yuhang

Your name was Chuanfang, courtesy name Xin Yuan. You were a native of Tai'an, Shandong. As a young man, you were selected as a student of the Beiyang Military Academy and sent to the Japanese Military Academy. You joined the Chinese Revolutionary Alliance. You were highly regarded by your fellow students, Zhu Tengyue, Li Genyuan, and Zhao Hengti. The Alliance's mission was to protect the nation and resist foreign invaders. You upheld this for ten years without wavering. When you governed Jiangsu, Shi Congbin led six thousand White Russians from Jinan to fight. You defeated them at Guzhen, capturing Shi Congbin and the White Russian chieftain Nie Qia Yefu, whom you immediately executed as a warning, saying, "I will not allow people to slaughter each other with foreigners." Later, forced by the Southern Army, you retreated to Jinan. You still commanded forty thousand soldiers. The consul stationed in Qingdao requested to assist in recovering lost territory with two divisions, vowing not to seek reward. The envoy came three times. You, mindful of the reasons for the downfall of the Song and Ming dynasties, firmly declined. You did not regret even after the defeat. It can be said that you did not break your promise to the Alliance. However, you were ultimately assassinated by Shi Congbin's daughter. While there may be much debate in the Confucian classics and laws about sons avenging their fathers, your execution of Shi Congbin was clearly a just punishment. You possessed a heroic and outstanding nature. In warfare, you were skilled at using few to control many. When speaking to people, your words flowed freely, and you could continue for an entire day. After graduating from the military academy and returning, you served as a training officer in the Beiyang Second Division, rising through the ranks to become the commander of the Sixth Regiment. In the third year of the Republic, the bandit Bai Lang Xuan rebelled in Henan, causing numerous defeats for the government troops. The court ordered a joint suppression by five provinces. The bandits traveled over a hundred miles a day, outstripping the pace of infantry and cavalry. You marched through heavy rain at double speed, attacking and annihilating their forces at Shangcheng. Bai Lang Xuan fled, and you became famous. You rose to the rank of division commander and served as the garrison commander of Pu Xian, Shi Yi, Xin Jia Pu, and Tong, as well as the Commander-in-Chief of the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. Subsequently, you served as the military governor of Fujian and Zhejiang, promoted to the inspector-general of Fujian and Zhejiang, appointed as a general of the army, and awarded the title of General Ke Wei. You commanded the military affairs of five provinces: Zhejiang, Fujian, Jiangsu, Anhui, and Jiangxi. During your one year in Zhejiang and Jiangsu, you never increased taxes due to military expenses. You repaid over three million in old debts for Zhejiang and over nine million for Jiangsu. You saved Jiangsu fifty thousand a month in military expenses. You reorganized seven million in public debt and abolished over ten kinds of harsh taxes. Since the establishment of the Republic, no other general has been like you in terms of thrift and benefiting the people. Although you later suffered defeats, the people of Wu and Yue did not forget your virtue. Your defeat of Shi Congbin was at the request of the elders of Shandong, Huai, and Xu. At that time, the White Russians Nie Qia Yefu and Bukes Nie Jiafo were skilled at operating armored vehicles. Shi Congbin recommended them to the military governor Zhang Zongchang of Shandong, who formed an armored vehicle unit of five. He recruited six thousand White Russians to serve under them and led the Han army south. The White Russians killed, raped, and plundered day and night, and few in the Huai and Si regions were spared. You used twenty thousand soldiers to defend Guzhen. Before the battle, the people seized the opportunity to destroy the railroad tracks. When the enemy arrived, you deployed your troops to surround them on both flanks and used heavy artillery to meet them head-on. All the armored vehicles collapsed. The military vehicles behind them, three in a row, retreated and collided with each other, unable to stop. You then used both flanks to shoot at them from left and right, inflicting a great defeat. The people watching cheered and celebrated along the roads. You pursued and captured Shi Congbin and Nie Qia Yefu and brought them back. You released all the captured officers and soldiers, executing only the two. At that time, the people of Shandong asked to take advantage of the victory and descend on Jinan, but you did not agree. However, the White Russian army was abolished from then on. The world often praises you for these three things, but none was as fierce as your elimination of filth at Guzhen. Since the founding of the Republic, the Revolutionary Alliance had changed its name and merged and split numerous times, and those who were distant could not even recall their oaths. When the Southern Allied Army rose in Guangdong, it was originally a major branch of the Alliance, but it was far removed from the initial assembly. The later recruits were frivolous and disrespectful to the old comrades. After you defeated Shi Congbin, your power grew daily. You began to oversee the military affairs of five provinces. The people between Wu and Chu looked up to you as their leader. Guangdong was also tense, and they once sent an envoy to seek peace, unaware of your inherent integrity. You believed that Guangdong had embraced the evil schemes of communism and that the Red Russians Borodin and Galen were secretly in charge. We record your old righteousness. The Southern Army had already captured Hanyang. You rushed to save it, leading your troops out of Jiujiang and engaging in battle, but you were taken advantage of. Returning to Jiangning, you knew that the upper reaches could not be defended and reluctantly sought assistance from Zhang Zuolin. Zuolin sent Zongchang and Chu Yupu with a hundred thousand soldiers to aid. The troops were disorganized, and you were ultimately defeated. Jiangnan completely fell. Retreating north, you held out for half a year. You again crossed the Yangtze River with a lone army and won several victories. Your troops reached Longtan, but reinforcements did not arrive, and you retreated into Shandong. You built a defense at Dawenkou for Zongchang, spending over a million. You camped west of it, entrusting Zongchang to defend it himself. While the battle was raging, Dawenkou fell, and you turned your army around. Your rejection of the □□ consul: you quoted the words of former President Li, "It is better to be subjugated by our compatriots than to fall into the hands of foreign invaders," to inform Zuolin. Zuolin also listened to your words and ordered the troops to withdraw through Yuguan to Huanggu Village, where they were ambushed and killed by □□ assassins. The advantages and disadvantages of things cannot be predicted in advance, but you were able to use your will to make Zuolin understand the greater righteousness. It can be said that you loved people with virtue. After you disbanded your army, you fled to Shenyang and lived there for four years. When Japan invaded Shenyang, you returned to Tianjin, living in seclusion and devoting yourself to Buddhism. You never spoke of national affairs again for another four years. In the winter of the twenty-fourth year, while listening to a sermon at the Jushilin Temple, you encountered Shi Congbin's daughter, who shot you in the back, the bullet exiting through your chest, and you died. You were fifty-one years old. You were married to Madame Zhang, followed by Madame Zhou. You had four sons: Jia Zhen, Jia Jun, Jia Yu, and Jia Qin, and three daughters. In April of the following year, you were reburied in Tai'an. When you were alive, you once said to your son, "When I commanded troops, I shared their joys and hardships. I have never used a single arrow against a foreign country, and this is my regret." You also established many good policies. Because your great integrity was based entirely on the resolutions of the Revolutionary Alliance, and your children and subordinates did not fully understand, I have specially recorded your character and the origins of your aspirations and actions. The inscription reads:

Those brave warriors! Men of dragon-like talents! Descendants of Fusang! Though talented, they are not of our race! I would rather kill enemies to protect the people than seek aid to survive. Therefore, the highest punishments must be used, and military strategies must be followed. In this divided land, alas, there is no way to exert one's strength. In this chaotic world, there is no justice. Let misfortune come from the evil gate. Believing in the righteous path, even lying dead is not enough to express it.

Correction: In last week's "Mourning Zhu Biaoyun" article, the ending "Xianci Temple in Suzhou" was mistakenly written. It should be "San Xian Ci Alley in Suzhou." We hereby correct this.

— Dai De

Phlegm is a secretion of the lungs. When the trachea has inflammatory symptoms, secretion increases, resulting in increased phlegm and frequent coughing. Therefore, if the lungs are healthy, phlegm will be minimal; conversely, it is a sign of lung disease.

Excessive phlegm often originates from colds and is most likely to induce ailments such as pulmonary tuberculosis and pneumonia. Therefore, whether it is a cold with coughing, phlegm and wheezing in the elderly, it is imperative to seek a radical cure promptly.
