Book Club

A Brief Discussion on the Progress of Biology in China in Recent Years 184

— Guangyu

Mr. Emil Bretschneider said: "The Chinese do not show a talent for observing nature, nor do they possess a sincere desire to seek the truth. These two qualities are essential for naturalists, yet the people of this country lack them. Chinese writing is often inaccurate, leading to ambiguity, and the Chinese tend to be fond of the strange, holding extremely naive views." This is a view from a position of idealism, dissecting very clearly the reasons why China has historically lacked biology. However, in the last ten years or so, biological research in China has progressed rapidly, already occupying a considerable position in the world of academia. So, why have our talent for observing nature and our enthusiasm for seeking the truth become so apparent now? This is naturally due to different social relations. Mr. Elsworth Huntington believes that Chinese farmers often encounter disasters and live in hardship, so they tend to be stingy and narrow-minded. From this, it can be inferred that in ancient China, because it was stagnant in an agricultural society, the capacity for production was weak, and obtaining a fulfilling life was difficult. Even those who were called wealthy were often unaware of the difficulty of survival and only thought about fame and profit all day long, and would not open their minds to scientific research. Therefore, biology would not develop until the capitalist society gradually emerged in China today.

Biology in books has been imported into China for decades. However, the study of biology through the observation of real objects and based on experiments has only a history of over a decade. This can be traced back to the establishment of the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society of China in the eleventh year of the Republic of China. Since then, only fifteen years have passed, but considerable achievements have already been made. In addition to the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society of China, research institutions include the Jing Sheng Biological Research Institute established in Beiping in the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, the National Central Research Institute's Natural History Museum (renamed the Institute of Zoology and Botany in the twenty-second year) established in Nanjing in the same year, the Beiping Research Institute's Institute of Zoology and Botany established in Beiping in the eighteenth year, and the Biological Research Institute of the China Western Academy of Sciences established in Beibei, Ba County, Sichuan in the twentieth year. Major well-known universities such as Central, Zhongshan, Peking, Tsinghua, Wuhan, Shandong, Zhejiang, Jinling, Yenching, and Lingnan have all established biology departments for specialized or regional research. In addition to the Science Society of China, academic societies include the Natural History Society of Beiping, the Chinese Zoological Society, the Chinese Botanical Society, the Chinese Physiological Society, the Marine Biological Society of Qingdao, and the Insect Interest Society of Nantong. Publications include the series reports of the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society of China, the series reports of the Jing Sheng Biological Research Institute, the series publications of the Agricultural and Forestry Botanical Research Institute of National Zhongshan University, and various other magazines and monographs. Most of these publications are written in Western languages and exchanged with famous research institutions and scholars around the world. In the case of the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society of China alone, there are more than five hundred such exchanges, which shows its attention to the world.

However, as far as general school education and general public knowledge are concerned, the research achievements of the above-mentioned research institutions and universities are still too focused on the profound and neglect popularization. This is because they have not yet been able to supply the textbooks used by general schools and the reading materials needed by the general public, and they still have to let the various bookstores fulfill this responsibility. Therefore, the progress of biological research in China in recent years, in terms of the profound, should be attributed to the above-mentioned research institutions and universities, and in terms of popularization, the contributions of the various bookstores should not be ignored either.

In recent years, the call for saving the country through science has become very loud. Biology inherently does not have many direct uses in saving the country, but in terms of indirect relations, agriculture, medicine, fisheries, organic chemistry, and so on all need to be based on biological research. Moreover, since Darwin established the theory of evolution, it has had a greater impact on human thought than any other theory in the past seventy years. Therefore, in this extraordinary period, popularizing biological knowledge to the general public is still a very important task.

China originally had no science, no biology. At this moment when biological research is just flourishing and beginning to achieve results, it is especially important to find ways to popularize the essence of these achievements to the general public, so that the general public can become the backing for in-depth research. Therefore, we believe that the biology books that various bookstores should publish now, in addition to good textbooks, should also pay attention to two aspects. One aspect is works like "Biological Sketches," recently recommended by the "Science" magazine, which "can both describe scientific facts and have literary flavor," which can break the general public's long-held notion that scientific books are dry and uninteresting, and unconsciously accept scientific influence. In addition to "Biological Sketches," this category of books includes "Flowers, Birds, Insects, and Fish," "Animal Anecdotes," "Birds and Literature," "Insect Talks," and "The Life of Insects" published by Kaiming Bookstore, all of which are good books worth recommending. The other category is large reference books based on Chinese materials, such as dictionaries, atlases, and rich taxonomic books. This type of book has not yet existed, which is what the publishing industry should strive to do in the future.

"Note": Regarding dictionaries, although there are already books such as the "Great Dictionary of Botany" and the "Great Dictionary of Zoology" on the market, because they are completely based on Japanese materials and were published a long time ago, general scholars deeply regard them as impractical. In the atlas category, there are the "Chinese Plant Atlas," "Chinese Fern Atlas," "Illustrated Guide to Common Trees in Hebei," and "Illustrated Guide to Common Fish in Hebei" published by the Jing Sheng Biological Research Institute, all of which have very exquisite content. However, the materials are few and the prices are high, so they are not suitable for general public use.

"Fulfilling a Long-Cherished Wish" 185

— Zhou Weiqun

"...Concentrating my mind and racking my brains, I finally gained a thorough understanding and glimpsed the mysteries of truth, experiencing endless interest..."

I remember when I was in middle school, the teacher only told me that the sum of the three angles of a triangle is equal to two right angles, and I never heard that it was less than or greater than two right angles. Perhaps the teacher himself did not know. When I entered university, a teacher happened to mention in class that in non-Euclidean geometry, the sum of the three angles of a triangle is less than or greater than two right angles; however, he did not explain the reason. At that time, I found it very strange, thinking that the sum of the three angles of a triangle being equal to two right angles was not only theoretically unquestionable, but also had been tested and verified hundreds of times in practice. How could it become a problem? If it is said to be less than or greater than two right angles, what reasons can it be based on? Leaving the reasons aside for the moment, the facts clearly do not match. Moreover, geometry is such a precise science. If theorems proven in geometry are still unreliable, how much credible reasoning can there be in the world? However, since non-Euclidean geometry has been generally recognized, it certainly would not talk nonsense. My curiosity could not restrain itself, and I had to study non-Euclidean geometry to see what skills it possessed that it dared to overturn right and wrong and make such an astonishing strange argument. Therefore, I looked for it domestically and abroad, buying one, two, three, and four books on non-Euclidean geometry written by several scholars. Unfortunately, at first, I could not understand them no matter how much I read. On the surface, it seemed like I understood, but in my heart, I still did not understand. I endured it. If I didn't understand today, I would read it again tomorrow. If I still didn't understand tomorrow, I would continue the day after tomorrow. After several days of continuous reading, I still didn't understand, so I put it aside and read it later. This went on intermittently for a long time. Concentrating my mind and racking my brains, I finally gained a thorough understanding one day, glimpsed the mysteries of truth, and experienced endless interest. I believe that people who study ordinary geometry should not fail to understand non-Euclidean geometry. If they do not understand non-Euclidean geometry, not only is their knowledge shallow and limited, but they also do not know what geometry is (What is Geometry?). They only remember many theorems, but theorems are not of much value. Because I have seen many incomprehensible books on non-Euclidean geometry, I suffered a lot. When I couldn't understand them, I thought that after I had thoroughly understood them, I would definitely compile a book on non-Euclidean geometry that would be easy for people to understand. Now that I have gained entry to the subject, I am fulfilling my long-cherished wish by compiling this "An Elementary Explanation of Non-Euclidean Geometry." Geometry is a deductive science. The most basic and important thing is the clarification of principles. Once the principles are clarified, there are not many difficulties below. Therefore, this small book focuses on clarifying the principles. I have explained in detail the places that I found difficult to understand and that had to be thoroughly understood when I was learning. As long as someone who has studied ordinary geometry and has a relatively precise mind can understand my book. It is especially suitable for high school graduates or third-year high school students who have studied analytical geometry to read this book. Deficiencies and errors are inevitable. I would be grateful for any corrections from readers.

(Editor's Note) Mr. Zhou wrote this article at the beginning of his book "An Elementary Explanation of Non-Euclidean Geometry" to tell us how he endured hardship and persevered, how he made up his mind to write and facilitate future scholars, and how he was careful and thorough in fulfilling his long-cherished wish. Anyone who reads this article will be moved by his spirit! We would like to contribute this to readers who aspire to study knowledge.

An Elementary Explanation of Non-Euclidean Geometry, written by Zhou Weiqun, 20 cents

Introduction to Advanced Mathematics, written by Zhou Weiqun, 1.40 yuan

Mathematical Fun, written by Liu Xunyu, 80 cents

A Critical Review of "Qu Yuan" 186

— Xiao Shunu

Written by Guo Moruo, published by Kaiming Bookstore, priced at 45 cents

If we want to explore Chinese literature and promote the Chinese literary revolution, we should be aware of a great revolutionary poet, Qu Yuan! Indeed, as a nobleman from the South, he fully accepted the temperament of popular art, created and adhered to his own poetic style, and boldly overthrew the aristocratic literature of the Taige style, leaving the most glorious page in the history of Chinese literature. If we have a love for literature, we cannot but first recognize this extraordinary poet with keen sensibility and understand his works to a considerable extent.

However, the problem arises from this: because Qu Yuan is already more than two thousand years away from us, all material evidence of his existence has disappeared, and the literature before the Biography of Qu Yuan in the Records of the Grand Historian is so scarce. Because of the omissions in the details of the Biography of Qu Yuan and the alterations made by later generations, some people even doubt Qu Yuan's existence. People like Ji Ping and Hu Shizhi have suspected that Qu Yuan may not have existed at all. Now their questions can be answered clearly in the book "Qu Yuan" written by Mr. Guo Moruo.

This book is divided into three chapters. The first chapter discusses in detail the existence of Qu Yuan and the criticism of the skeptical theory. The second chapter analyzes the age and authenticity of Qu Yuan's works. The third chapter describes the inheritance of Qu Yuan's thought and his artistic attitude. The author of this book not only relies on the materials in the books, but also looks for evidence in bronze inscriptions and oracle bone inscriptions. For example, he infers that "朕皇考曰伯庸" in the poem "Li Sao" is Qu Yuan's appellation for his father's name, based on the fact that it is common to see descendants referring to their fathers and grandfathers by their names in bronze inscriptions. How powerful is this argument! Here, the author also elaborately reveals Qu Yuan's family background, which not only makes us believe in his existence, but also fortunately allows us to understand the exact date of birth and death of this great poet from Guo's precise calculations of ancient calendars!

In the past, there were different opinions on his birthday. According to Liu Shipei's "Glimpse of Ancient Calendars," calculated according to the Xia calendar, his birthday should be on the 21st day of the first month of the 27th year of the false King Xuan of Chu (the 26th year of King Xian of Zhou - 343 BC). According to Chen's "Chronology of Zisi's Birth and Death," calculated according to the Zhou calendar, it would be on the 22nd day of the third month of the same year. However, Guo said that "his date of birth is seen in the 'Li Sao', '摄提贞于孟陬兮，惟庚寅吾以降', he was born in the first month of the year when Jupiter was in 寅,庚寅. According to the Preface to 'Lushi Chunqiu', '维秦八年，岁在鹑火', we know that 239 BC was the year of Shen. Pushing up, the 29th year of King Xuan of Chu (28th year of King Xian of Zhou) in 341 BC should be the year of Yin, but the first month of that year was small, 庚申朔, and there was no day of Gengyin... Jupiter surpassed the constellation once every 82.6 years. During that period, it surpassed the constellation once, and the year of Yin should be 340 BC. The first month of that year was small, 甲申朔, and Gengyin was the seventh day, which is consistent with the 'Li Sao'." I believe no one will have any doubts after reading his precise deduction.

Guo's invention is not limited to this. He pointed out from bronze inscriptions that the "Luan Yue" at the end of the Chu Ci is "Ci Yue". He also clarified from oracle bone inscriptions that "Heavenly Questions" is not a difficult work made by later generations - as Mr. Hu Shizhi said, but Qu Yuan's own work. The ironclad evidence he presented makes us feel the love and affection for the great poet.

Guo's book should be a rare specialized work. Recently, he said that this was originally written for the Kaiming Middle School Student Series, but it was too difficult, so he added an appendix "Modern Translation of 'Li Sao'" to make it independent (see "Qu Yuan's Era" in the February issue of Literature). Here, we should not easily let go of the translation in this appendix; I believe that anyone with a cultivation in old literature knows that translating ancient poems into modern poems is indeed a difficult task, because their language is obscure and it is often difficult to express them consistently. For example, "Li Sao" says "解佩紱以结言兮，吾令蹇修以为理". Wang Yi's commentary says that "'理' is '理分理也，述求婚之意也'", but still cannot point out its clear concept. Such a translation is certainly difficult: but Guo based it on the following "理弱而媒拙" and the chapter "Nine Chapters" "理弱而媒不通", and "Thinking of Beauty" "令謇荔以为理！囡芙蓉以为媒", proving that the matchmaker is called "理", "盖古者提婚人与媒妁人有别". Therefore, he translated it very clearly into the following verse: "我把兰佩解下来拜托了蹇修，我请他謇了去为我向她求爱." This is enough to show that the translator spent a lot of deep research. However, I think it is still necessary to add some explanation, otherwise the general public will not be able to understand how the orchid pendant is related to courtship. Now, according to the "Da Dai Li", "蔫氏之机，芗氏之藉", note that "兰柱香草名". "Materia Medica" says "'蘅' is fragrant, that is, Du Heng". Tang poetry: "'情人一去无穷已，欲赠蘅香恨不逢'". Therefore, "解佩紱以结言" means that men and women give fragrant objects to each other as a token of affection! In my opinion, "佩紱" is "香幃". Wang Yi said "'幃谓之香缨，赠香囊也'". "香囊" is also a "香囊", which both men and women wore in ancient times. The marriage is called "结藕", "亲以自思" in the "Guo Feng" of the Book of Songs. "香缨" and "容臭" are also the same thing. The note in "Li Neize" says "容臭，香物也. 助以形容之饰，以缨系之". Hong Xingzu's "Supplement to the Chu Ci" says "古者男女均佩容臭，香物也". This kind of fragrant pendant is related to sexual love. Fan Qin's poem "Ding Qing" in the Jin Dynasty says "'何以致叩叩？香囊系肘后'". The ancient story of "Peacock Flies Southeast" is even clearer, saying "'红罗复斗帐，四角垂香囊'". According to Li Tiaoyuan's "Notes on Guangdong" in the Qing Dynasty, volume 4, the people of South Vietnam, whenever men and women are about to have an affair, they offer a fragrant bag in front of the gods, and often get what they want. Enough, a long story! However, from this, it can be seen that Guo's translation has a full understanding of the original text.

In addition, Guo still has a question about the lines "名余曰正则兮，字余曰灵均" in the "Li Sao". If it is said that Qu Yuan is describing his name and style name, why doesn't he say "名平字原"? In fact: "Li Sao" is a true work from his later years after being exiled. - The people of Chu were influenced by the religious beliefs of the Yin people. It can be known from the frequent activities of shamans in his original works. This is because he was full of grievances, which made him more urgently need metaphysical relief. Doesn't the "Li Sao" say? ""愿依彭咸之遗则"",众山海经海内西红及大荒西经有""巫彭""巫咸""之名"",Wang Yi says""彭咸楚大夫，谏其君不听，自投水而死"". It is also said that ""巫咸古神巫也，当殷中宗之世"". Then Qu Yuan intended to become a shaman. "Li Sao" calls himself ""正则"" based on the ""彭咸之遗则"",and the style name ""灵均"" is taken from the meaning of the witches. ""和和"" and ""氛正"" are also shaman names. If my conjecture is not wrong. I hope Guo will add corrections when the book is republished.

I would like to introduce this book to young people with great respect. I firmly believe that it will arouse their interest in studying this great poet and his works.

The Literaryization of Science 187

— Wang Meiye

——Introducing "Lectures on Meteorology"——

Most people love to read literary books but not scientific books. The reason for this is that studying science requires a precise mind and painstaking thinking, so they feel that science is boring and that scientific subjects give them a headache. In fact, we must know that no matter what kind of knowledge you study, "painstaking thinking" is inevitable. If you are afraid of painstaking thinking, you have no hope of succeeding in your studies. Taking literature as an example, if you do not think hard when reading, you will overlook the wonderful descriptions and the tortuous meanings. The reason why it is now felt that reading literary books is not difficult but reading scientific books is difficult is nothing more than the interest of the words.

Science is the key to improving human life. The modern world is a world of science. If the science of a country is not developed, this country is in danger of being swallowed up. Therefore, although we who are born today do not want to be great scientists, it is impossible not to know some common scientific knowledge in daily life.

Because the words in scientific books are mostly dry and boring, everyone does not like to read them, and they do not have common scientific knowledge in daily life. Living in today's scientific world, the danger of the future is really unbearable! According to a doctor, there are many medicines that are bitter and difficult to take, so they are specially mixed with sweet fruit juice to make people not feel difficult. I believe that scientific books, even if they are dry and tasteless, must be written in interesting words, just like adding sweet fruit juice to bitter medicine. I envy the good fortune of foreign children, who can read scientific works written in a literary style, such as Fabre's "Chemical Fables", "Stories of Science" (both of which have been translated by Kaiming Bookstore), "Our Earth", "Insect Records", and so on. When people read them, it is like reading novels, and scientific knowledge has been unknowingly drilled into the readers' minds.

Apart from a few translated books, there are not many of these interesting scientific works in China. But no matter how well you translate the translated books, they are foreign products after all. The national conditions of foreign countries are not the same as ours, and the materials of foreign countries are somewhat estranged from us Chinese. It is best for us Chinese to use their methods to make some domestic products ourselves. This book, "Lectures on Meteorology", is our exquisite domestic product. The beauty of the writing can be compared with Fabre!

This book is divided into nine lectures, which express the meteorology of wind, cloud, rain, dew, frost, snow, cold, heat, etc. by borrowing Mr. Mi's story to two nephews named Zijun and Zijie, so that we can gain meteorological knowledge after reading it. Originally, there were very few books on meteorology published in China, and the study of meteorology was as stuffy as learning mathematics. Because there are not many books published, and because the materials are boring, Chinese people do not pay attention to it as if it were rotten copper and iron. Try to hold a scholar who has read books for more than ten years and ask "How many kinds of clouds are there?" I believe his answer is "Two kinds, white clouds and black clouds", and he will have to laugh at you for asking a silly question, thinking that this is common sense that a four- or five-year-old child knows. But is his answer correct? We turn over the meteorology books and know that there are thirteen kinds of clouds, with different shapes and heights, and we also know that clouds are good at changing - the real change is not the change that we look up and see like a dog, and after a while it becomes like a person - each kind of cloud, becomes thicker and thinner, or may disappear, or may become another kind of cloud. The poems of great poets often use wind, cloud, rain, dew, frost, snow, etc. as poetic materials, so even those who study literature can get an extra kind of interest after reading this book and reminiscing about the chants of the great poets.

This book only uses the style of storytelling to describe the principles of meteorology, and there are also many places that can be experimented with, and pictures that can be referred to, so that readers can understand it more easily.

Everyone says that reading scientific books is dull and boring, but the authors, like doctors, can mix sweet things in bitter medicine, and naturally they can eliminate "dullness and boredom". Now that I have found such a good book, I would like to introduce it to readers. At the same time, I hope that the general writers can pay attention to this point, make science literary, change the idea that everyone has always disliked reading scientific books, and make the silent scientific community lively. This is really a kind of happiness in the reading world, and to put it bigger, it is the happiness of mankind! The far-sighted and energetic Kaiming Bookstore, may you continue to work hard after this book, I think my little hope will eventually be realized!

February 10, 1935, in Beiping

Imitating the Ancients - Reading at Night by Lamplight - The Night Before the Big Exam 188

— Yuanzhizhai Paper

Introducing a Japanese Self-Study Book 189

— Zheng

Japanese Grammar Explained by Aihua

Published by Kaiming Bookstore, priced at one yuan and forty cents

Opening recent newspapers, we often see advertisements for morning and evening cram schools in the enrollment columns. Analyzing these advertisements, almost half belong to Japanese language specialization courses. From this, we can imagine how our country's youth are paying attention to the work of "knowing yourself and your enemy" in their spare time. However, when we try to search for some suitable Japanese language textbooks from various publishers, as far as I know, there seem to be very few books for beginners that can integrate lessons, grammar, and exercises together with detailed explanations. General textbooks often neglect one thing for another. As for those for advanced learners and self-study, they are even scarcer. Therefore, many schools often adopt oral teaching methods or directly use Japanese books. This inevitably leads to errors, omissions, and inconsistencies.

Among the few good books on learning Japanese, I would like to introduce one that is more satisfying and suitable for teaching and self-study: "Japanese Grammar Explained" by Aihua.

The author said in the "Preface" of this book: "The author has two important intentions in writing this book: first, to enable readers to thoroughly understand the meaning of Japanese; second, to make it easier for readers to understand translation methods." I am unwilling to praise him for "being able to break through the difficulties felt by scholars in the past" just because he said these two sentences. Because many books are just blowing their own horns in the preface, but their content completely disappoints people. Let's honestly open the book and take a closer look:

The book uses Aesop's Fables translated by the Japanese Morning News Xiaobo as the text, which is both short and interesting. Most of these stories are already known to readers, making it easier to increase comprehension. But this is not its special feature. Its only good thing is that it can use the annotations of each sentence to give many examples, even listing them in tables, to meticulously explain the grammar of each word in the sentence, so that readers learn unintentionally, just like taking a bite of a steamed bun and eating the filling inside. Except for the easiest words and phrases, almost every sentence in the text is translated and explained in detail, so that beginners can fully understand it after reading it. After each lesson, there are also idioms and idiomatic expressions that readers should memorize, so that they can be specially memorized. From this, we can imagine how hard the author is working for the readers.

In addition, the translation methods of each sentence in the book also have many unique points. It is a pity that due to space and printing inconveniences, I cannot give a few examples. The whole book has a total of thirty lessons, totaling three hundred and fifty-four pages. If you study hard, you can finish reading it in at most three months.

Finally, I hope that Mr. Aihua or other scholars who have a deep understanding of Japanese will publish more books of this kind, so that people who are new to Japanese will not feel a lack of reading materials.

Letter from the Ordinary Education Department of the Ministry of Education to Various Bookstore Operators 190

Respectfully, after reviewing the revised and promulgated schedule of teaching subjects and hours for primary and secondary schools, the curriculum standards for various subjects in all primary and secondary schools will be modified accordingly. In order to enable primary and secondary schools across the country to obtain perfect textbooks and to facilitate the smooth progress of the business of various bookstore operators, the Ministry issued an invitation from the Department on the 27th of last month to bookstore operators to hold a discussion meeting at the Ministry. Several resolutions were made and the records were sent to the Ministry for filing. With the approval of the Vice Minister, the relevant records are hereby attached for your information and compliance.

Records of the Discussion Meeting of Bookstore Operators

Time: February 27, 25th year of the Republic of China, morning

Location: Conference Room, Ministry of Education

Attendees: Wang Yunwu, Lu Fei Bohong, and thirteen others

Chairman: Gu Shusen

Reporting Matters

(1) Textbooks that must be edited immediately are:

(1) Civics for the first and second grades of junior and senior high school

(2) Mathematics for the second grade of senior high school, levels A and B (If it is impossible to publish a book, please ask experts to select several textbooks and make slight changes to the order of the teaching materials in accordance with the newly revised curriculum standards. Level B books may also be used temporarily for Level A books, but with some parts deleted)

(3) Physiology and hygiene for junior high school

(2) Simplification of Review Procedures

(1) Within one year from the date of promulgation of the revised curriculum standards, textbooks for each subject may be submitted for review separately, but they will be approved for trial use first and then formally approved when all reviews are completed in the future.

(2) The above three types of textbooks that must be edited may be submitted for review in printed form within six months from the date of promulgation of the revised curriculum standards.

(3) The Compilation and Translation Museum should expedite the review and complete the review within about one month.

(3) Changes to the Effective Period of Approval

(1) Any textbooks that have been approved but whose content is completely different from the newly revised curriculum standards will become invalid immediately.

(2) If a small part is different and cannot be modified in time, it will become invalid by the end of June next year.

(3) Those that expire this year will be extended to the end of June next year.

(4) Those whose content is completely the same will remain valid for their original term without any changes.

(5) Textbooks for primary schools whose content has not changed will be extended for one year.

(4) Changes to the Date Filled in on the Approval Certificate

The effective period of approval should be calculated based on six semesters. If the approval is made after the start of the semester, the textbooks for the spring and autumn seasons should be calculated separately from the next semester or the next school year for a total of six semesters as the effective period of approval.

Telegraphic Special Edition

Removing Misunderstandings Lies in Questioning 191

— Zhen

We cannot avoid misunderstandings in our interactions with the world, and we cannot avoid indignation when things go against our wishes. If we question, then the truth will be revealed and misunderstandings will be resolved. Otherwise, speculation, doubts in our hearts, arbitrary criticism, or ridicule will cause misunderstandings between each other. On the receiving end, they may not even know why this happened? There is no way to find the root cause, is this not a matter of regret? Leaving aside other matters, let's talk about telecommunications:

Telecommunications is one of the public utilities and is closely related to the interests of users - senders, receivers, or telephone users. If the telephone is not working, or the telegram is not delivered or delayed, then the user will naturally be dissatisfied. However, whether the reason for the failure or delay is due to the negligence of the telegraph office cannot be determined without questioning or investigation. If it is confirmed that the telegraph office made a mistake, then the telegraph office will handle it according to the telegraph or telephone business regulations and various telecommunications laws, and at the same time, it should refund the extra expenses to the user and express its apologies. If the error is not in the telegraph office, then the telegraph office is not responsible legally or morally.

If users have opinions, they should not ask the telegraph office or conduct an investigation, but instead spread what they have encountered and suffered to the outside world, saying, "The telegram is not delivered," or "The telephone is not working." From the perspective of knowledgeable people, this person and these words are quite lacking in reason, unclear about the regulations, and not what the telegraph office wants.

I read a news item in a Nanjing newspaper entitled "Telephone Cannot Be Connected." The sender, Mr. So-and-so, sent a telegram to the Xiaguan Telegraph Office at 11 p.m. one night, but no one answered the door, and the telegram was not sent. He then sent a letter to a newspaper to describe his experience. After investigation by the business inspector, the office did not close at night, the sender did not need to knock, and the staff were on duty day and night, so there was no reason why no one would answer the door. Moreover, it was found that several merchants sent telegrams at that time on that night, which can be proven by the telegraph records. It can be seen that Mr. So-and-so knocked on the wrong door and could not enter, so the telegram could not be sent. We express our deep sympathy, but it is a pity that we did not investigate and immediately concluded that "the telegram cannot be delivered," causing a misunderstanding.

On the part of the telegraph office, we are eager for people in the society to tell us the actual situation of sending and receiving telegrams and calls. Therefore, we have set up business inspectors and held communication inspection sessions. We especially hope that people in the society will understand the regulations for sending and receiving telegrams and calls. Therefore, we issue this publication, give regular broadcasts, and send various regulations. If various sectors send bureaus or use telephones to inquire about various regulations or procedures, we will sincerely welcome them. Only by removing all misunderstandings and explaining all doubts can we achieve the goal of close cooperation.

Supplement to the Writing and Charging Methods for the Address and Name of the Recipient of Chinese Telegrams 192

— Baozhen

Detailed regulations on the writing and charging methods for the address and name of the recipient of Chinese telegrams are already included in the current domestic telegraph business regulations. However, for Chinese private telegrams sent from a certain recipient to another person, for example, "Zhang Boyu c/o No. 5, Lane 538, Matte Hesituo Road, Shanghai, to Zeng Zhonggong," it is not clearly stipulated whether the words after "c/o" should be included in the recipient's address and name or in the telegram text when calculating the number of words. As a result, telegraph office clerks often still include words such as c/o or forwarding to someone in the telegram text when calculating the fee for the above telegrams submitted by the sender, as usual. It is now learned that in order to facilitate the sender, the Ministry of Communications has specially issued a notice to various telegraph offices to stipulate supplementary methods as follows:

(1) For Chinese private telegrams sent from a certain recipient to another person, regardless of whether the recipient's address and name are written in detail with words, or the address is replaced with a telephone number or a mailbox number, the second recipient's name should be allowed to be included in the recipient's address and name together with the word "c/o" or the two words "forward to." For example, (1) "Zhang Zhongchi c/o No. 288, Matte Hesituo Road, Shanghai, to Wang Shumei - I hope you will return to Ping quickly," (2) "Chen Zhiren c/o Nanjing Dialect (31788) to Ye Erheng - Has the money been remitted? Please reply by telegram," (3) "Huang Yongfu c/o Qingdao Mailbox (275) to Dai Shiquan - Qingmi...". The recipient's address and name in the first example above have a total of fifteen characters. According to the third item of Article 83 of the domestic telegraph business regulations, two characters are exceeded, so it should be charged as five characters (the place name of the receiving area is charged as two characters). The recipient's address and name in the second example do not exceed thirteen characters and can be charged as three characters according to the regulations. The recipient's address and name in the third example are all charged at four characters according to the regulations because it is a Chinese coded private telegram.

(2) For Chinese private telegrams sent from a registered household to another person, the nature is the same as those sent c/o a certain recipient and should be handled in the same way according to the regulations in the previous paragraph. The writing format stipulated in Article 45 of the domestic telegraph business regulations should also be supplemented as follows:

Registered word Receiving place name C/O someone Telegram

○○二二 Beiping C/O Wang Weicheng ...

The registration number and all the characters after the word "transfer", in the Chinese Mingyu private telegram, which do not exceed thirteen characters in total, or in the Chinese coded private telegram, which do not exceed fourteen characters in total, should be allowed to be charged as three characters or four characters respectively.

For Chinese telegrams with two or more recipient names, except for those marked by the sender with the words "send several copies" and charged, they should be handled according to the method of sending telegrams separately: those that are not marked by the sender, the telegraph office clerks often still list only the first recipient's name in the address and list the second recipient's name as the telegram text and charge by the number of words, as usual. For example, "Kang Minggang, Central Hotel, Daxinggong, Nanjing - Chen Guohua will come with you," the telegram will inevitably be inconsistent with the original intention. It is learned that the Ministry of Communications has also ordered all telegraph offices to allow the names of two or more recipients contained in the telegram to be included in the recipient's address and charged according to the regulations, but only if they belong to the same address.

After the implementation of the above supplementary methods, it will be convenient for all sectors, especially for telegrams, such as "Mr. Zou Guoliang and Ms. Jian Peihua, Dahuah Hotel, Shanghai - Congratulations on your happy wedding and wish you happiness without measure, Yongmei." The two recipient names in the telegram are included in the address, and there is no disadvantage of segmentation. The recipient's address and name in the telegram have a total of fourteen characters and should be charged as four characters according to the regulations. Since the sender of the telegram did not mark "send two copies", the receiving office only needs to send one copy to the first recipient when delivering the telegram. If the first recipient is not there, the telegram will be sent to the second recipient. This applies to those with two or more recipients by analogy.

Talking about Things that Senders Often Neglect 193

— Zhang Li

Since the publication of the Telegraphic Special Edition, it has indeed made many contributions to the outside world. Today, the telegraphic business is becoming increasingly closer to the public, and this cannot but be attributed to it. However, while there are many people who understand the telegraphic business and use telegrams as much as possible, there are still many who do not know how to send telegrams. I would like to use a corner of this publication to tell readers about the places that people who send and receive telegrams usually neglect.

1. Chinese Mingyu self-translators must add notes:

According to Article 42 of the Domestic Telegraph Business Regulations: "Chinese Mingyu private telegrams shall not only contain code words without text," the receiving clerks in various places must ask the sender to add text to this type of telegram without text, which is in accordance with the regulations. Often, due to unclear transmission by the servant or the sender's habit of sending official military telegrams, they do not write text even when occasionally sending ordinary telegrams. Even after many explanations, it is easy to cause unpleasantness or misunderstandings. I would like to reiterate this to remind senders to pay attention. The Ministry of Communications' intention in formulating this regulation is nothing more than to seek benefits for senders. Because if the sender does not add notes, there is no way to correct any errors in the interpretation of the code words. If notes have been added, the receiving clerk can check and correct them at any time, so that the recipient will not receive a telegram that is unreadable. This directly helps senders and receivers and indirectly contributes to the reputation of the telegraph office, thereby achieving the ultimate goal of telegraphs serving the people.

2. The telegraph receipt must state the sender's name and address

The sender's name and address must be written in detail on the telegram paper. If the telegram cannot be delivered properly, the sender can be notified according to the address written. Otherwise, the telegram cannot be delivered and the sender cannot be notified. Therefore, detailed notation of the sender's name and address is of great convenience to the sender.

It often happens that general commercial firms send telegrams with only one line of name or store number and often do not affix a seal. The telegraph office often accommodates and processes the telegrams for the convenience of the sender and immediately accepts them. However, from the perspective of commercial firms, this is actually dangerous! If unscrupulous elements impersonate the commercial firm and send telegrams to commit evil deeds and fraud, the telegraph office will not be responsible for any major losses incurred. Therefore, it is hoped that major commercial firms will pay attention and affix a seal when sending telegrams in the future. It is best to have a secret code and notify the authorities to check and verify, so as to be more solemn. (To be continued)

The Relationship between the Time Difference between China and Various Places in the World 194

— Ying

Since the successive opening of the direct circuits from the Ministry of Communications' International Radio Station to all parts of the world, international telegrams transmitted via Cgra are all extremely fast and accurate, and have been praised by all sectors. However, the speed of the telegram paper is based on the original sending time as the standard. Therefore, the "time" item is quite important on the telegram. It is found that the time in China and various places in the world, due to geographical relations, differs from the time in major cities in the world by tens of minutes or tens of hours, with varying differences. If you are not an expert in frequently used international telegrams, it may be difficult to understand the details. Now, in order to facilitate the investigation of the transmission time of international incoming telegrams, for the sake of universality, the time difference between China and various places in the world is listed separately on the left:

Explanation

When checking the transmission time of international incoming telegrams, you can use the above table. For those whose time is faster than China's time, subtract the faster time from the original sending time. For those whose time is slower, add the slower time. Then you can calculate it. For example, if a telegram from Tokyo, Japan, is sent at 9:15 and received at 10:15, then the transmission time is known to be two hours. That is, 10.15 - (9.15 - 1.00) = 2.00, 21.00 - (10.00 + 8.00) = 3.00, and so on.

Questions and Answers 195

This publication has a special column for questions and answers. People from all walks of life are welcome to ask questions about the procedures for sending and receiving telegrams and telephones, or about the telecommunications regulations that are not clear, or when there are questions about telecommunications common sense. This publication expresses its welcome and will answer them in detail.

1. Mr. Hu Kaiming from Tianjin asks: Our office has previously received many official telegrams in Mingyu (plain language) from various parties, which were all self-translated by me, which I found quite troublesome. Recently, the telegrams received have been translated and sent by the telegraph office, which is very convenient. However, there are cases where they are not translated. I don't know what the telegraph office's procedures are? Please advise.

(Answer) In order to show thoughtful service, the Ministry of Communications has specially ordered all bureaus that, from March 1, all incoming official telegrams in Ming code (plain code), except for cipher code, should be translated and delivered by the receiving office. If you receive a Mingyu official translation later, or an urgent, ordinary telegram, or a communication telegram, if it is not translated, please negotiate with the telegraph office.

2. Liu Zihe from Wuxian asks: A friend installed a telephone at the telephone office on January 14, and then removed it on February 18. The telephone office wants to charge two months' rent, is this legal?

(Answer) According to Article 36 of the Ministry of Communications' regulations on the operation of local telephones, "If a user installs a machine on or before the 15th of the month and removes the machine on or after the 16th, the rent will be calculated for the entire month." The telephone office's charge for two months' rent is not unreasonable.

3. Hua Wenxiu from Zhengxian asks: A long-distance telephone call has been notified and has already been transmitted, but the station has not been answered within the specified period. If the caller requests to cancel the number, how should it be handled?

(Answer) The cancellation fee should be waived, and all special force fees should be refunded.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

The Situation After the German Army Marched into the Rhineland 196

— Neng

After the German army suddenly marched into the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland the other day, all countries were shocked, especially France, which was preparing for war, mobilizing troops, and dispatching generals. As of now, the number of German troops arriving one after another has reached as many as 60,000. The situation of the war is in sight. A journalist from a certain country predicted that the European war would begin in the summer of next year, and people will secretly laugh at the error of observation.

According to the French government, there can be no negotiations as long as there is a German soldier stationed in the Rhineland. According to the German government, it is absolutely impossible to withdraw a single soldier. Moreover, the distance between the two countries is only a river apart. Not to mention cannons, even pistols can come into contact. Assuming that there is no possibility of war at this point, it is either foolish or crazy.

In fact, the beginning of the war depends entirely on the third party, Britain, and not on France. France believes that Germany's tearing up of the Locarno Treaty this time is a terrible thing, and fears that Germany will first station troops in the Rhineland, and secondly, take back the lost territory during the war. If this is not dealt with head-on, the consequences will be disastrous. Therefore, France believes that the seriousness of this incident lies here.

But what is Britain's attitude? Britain is determined not to have a second major war. There are two reasons for this: (1) In the Italian-Ethiopian War, although Britain expressed great dissatisfaction, it did not dare to use force to sanction it, let alone economic sanctions. Now there is the possibility of a British-Italian compromise. Moreover, in the Far East, since the Tokyo Incident in Japan, the means of aggression have become even more obvious. If the Franco-German War is added, it will inevitably create a situation of world war. These are all facts that are in sight.

(2) Examining the sudden march of the German army into the Rhineland, the Rhineland was originally German territory. It is a matter of course for German troops to be stationed on German territory. It cannot be said that Germany is taking excessive actions. Assuming that the army of Country A is stationed on the territory of Country B, or the army of Country B is stationed on the territory of Country C, that is wrong. Therefore, according to a Paris dispatch the other day, "Britain believes that Germany's re-stationing of troops in the Rhineland cannot be used as a basis for imposing sanctions on Germany, because Germany's actions are not of an aggressive nature." This is still a fair argument, but the French will definitely be very dissatisfied when they hear it.

France believes that the seriousness of this German violation of the Locarno Treaty cannot be overstated. In fact, looking back, I don’t know how many so-called treaties and alliances have already been torn up, and their violations are completely aggressive in nature. Therefore, the German army's re-stationing in the Rhineland is considered by the French to be a serious matter, but in the eyes of other countries, it is not uncommon.

Now Europe's response to Germany's abandonment will be moved to London for discussion, which shows that the situation is easing. Because the French are now excited and very fierce, it is not easy to have a level-headed discussion in this passionate environment. Therefore, it is a strategy to lure the tiger away from the mountain. This also shows Britain's dilemma. Therefore, the European war has not yet reached a mature stage, which can be seen from this.

Lantern Festival 197

— Fangzhou

Many families in Shirentou were busy for several days and nights. Huang Boshou went to the city to buy foreign yarn, red candles, and all the necessary sundries. Zhang Amao directed the construction of the lantern racks and directed the people who played the roles. Wu Xiaosan went to the major households to borrow the jewelry and costumes used for the horses in the parade, and the costumes in the local opera. The whole village was bustling as if something big had happened. The Huang Family Ancestral Hall, which was usually so deserted that ghosts could be caught, was almost crowded with people day and night these days. Some were splitting bamboo, some were building frames, some were pasting foreign yarn, some were painting flowers, and everyone was working in division of labor and cooperation, and everyone's heart was filled with a kind of exciting enzyme.

"What are you playing, Ah San?" Jin Sheng asked Sanhe like this two days before the lantern parade: "You must be ready!"

"No!" Sanhe smiled and shook his head.

"You play a henpecked husband, Sanhe, you are very good at saying dead words." Genbao took over and offered Sanhe his opinion.

"No, I want to play a clam catcher, and I want to ask your madam to play the clam spirit, what do you think?" Sanhe asked Genbao playfully.

"Then please ask your own Jade Emperor!"

"No, she's too old, the clam spirit should be young and beautiful."

"Okay, let's do this, you play a crab catcher, then call your wife to be an old crab, isn't this fresh and convenient?"

Many people laughed at what they said, and even Genbao himself laughed triumphantly, but Sanhe uninterestedly took off Genbao's new felt hat from his head and threw it to the door.

On the night of the lantern parade, the village was already full of a joyful atmosphere. Many children sneaked out of the back door as soon as they finished dinner. The sound of gongs, drums and firecrackers in the distance was faintly sent to the ears of every villager. The dogs in the village were howling and running wildly. A banquet for receiving the parade horses was set up in the Mengjiang Hall in front of the mountain. A large crowd of men, women, and children had already gathered on the not-so-wide open space in front.

The sky was pitch black, without stars or moon, but the hillsides on both sides were crowded with many people watching the parade horses. From the foot of Jilong Mountain to Huangye Ridge, there was almost no empty space to be found.

The parade of horses left the Huang Family Ancestral Hall and meandered along the gravel road and Meihua Bridge towards Huangye Ridge. The lights shone in the dark night, like a golden snake several miles long. The sounds of gongs, drums, and firecrackers had already broken the silence of the deep night, scaring the birds that lived in the woods and making them fly around in the dark.

— (Blow)

A-guo Army General Muruqi passed away on the 8th at the age of seventy. According to A-guan court's claim, he died of pneumonia. Tan Lao San said, "This old man will be angered to death even if he doesn't die of illness."

The US government stated that the dispute caused by Germany's abandonment of the Locarno Treaty in Europe has no impact on the United States. Therefore, the US government will never intervene in Germany's re-stationing of troops in the Rhineland. Tan Lao San said, "Pushing the moon out of the door and ignoring the frost on other people's roofs." The United States pushes the affairs of Germany and France completely away, but the United States also seems to have participated in the European war. Therefore, some people say that the United States' Monroe Doctrine is a half-open door. If there is a gap to take advantage of, then it says "I cannot sit idly by." If it is a bit awkward, then it immediately "revises the Neutrality Act," a brilliant move.

Pilgrims 199

— Li Xuan

When I was a child, around the third month, peach blossoms bloomed like a pink sea, and the snow melted into the green waves of wheat fields. The village roads in my hometown became lively.

A large reed mat shed was erected at the north entrance of the village, with several long tables and chairs inside. On the tables were ridiculously large gray earthenware teapots. A kind old man continuously poured lukewarm tea from a pot. Besides making tea and lighting incense, he squatted by the soft, damp roadside all day. When passersby approached the shed, the old man stood up, cracked his sunken mouth, and said with a smile:

Page 22

"You must be tired, have a cup of tea before continuing your journey."

When the walkers stood firm, they cupped their hands to the old man, unloaded the yellow packages from their backs, and placed them respectfully on the square table inside the shed, where a deity was enshrined. They respectfully stood the packages in the niche, picked up three incense sticks from the table, lit them from the black, smoky oil lamp, bowed to the deity, and inserted the incense into the incense burner. Turning around, they took a black earthenware bowl from the head of the long table, approached the mouth of the massive teapot that looked like it was pregnant, and poured out a bowl of thick, red tea swirling with many dark specks. They lifted it to their lips and gulped it down.

This teahouse was specifically for the pilgrims 'paying homage to the summit'. The travelers drank their fill of tea and rested on the long benches. Then, they carried their apricot-yellow packages again and cupped their hands to the old man, saying:

"See you on the way back, do you want anything from the mountains?"

"No, no, take it slow when climbing the winding path."

This kind old man never tired of seeing off each pilgrim, and the pilgrims flowed endlessly, intermittently walking along this road from the beginning of the third month.

Like these people traveling alone on mountain roads, who were running incense, they were very poor. Most were old couples in their eighties or nineties, sincerely worshiping the gods, and middle-aged bachelors who liked to gamble, along with mischievous young rascals who loved excitement. Wealthy people seized two-wheeled carts, bringing their wives and children, the carts loaded with cooked pork pancakes, white liquor, and playing cards. The cart driver cracked the long leather whip in his hand, driving the livestock forward. The family sat in the cart, playing cards for a while, drinking a few sips of strong liquor. When the young men were happy, they stole glances at the fashionable women in the carts ahead and behind. The older ones mostly liked to doze off or go to the Emperor's cart to gamble. The girls were generally more honest, occasionally glancing at the men, and if their mothers saw them, they would inevitably get scolded. The girls blushed and didn't dare to look up for a long time... Thus, like a vast picture of displaced people, they spent two days and one night approaching the foot of the mountain.

In addition, there were pilgrims fulfilling vows. They had all vowed to the Holy Mother of the North Tortoise Mountain peak for their relatives' unexpected disasters or illnesses, undertaking a cruel self-torture: the better ones dressed themselves as strangely shaped beasts, such as human-bodied, ox-headed or pig-headed monsters, or some kind of evil spirit. Once dressed, they left home and ran all the way to the mountain to burn incense before removing their costumes and turning back into humans.

The most pitiful were some old women who, to pray for the blessing of their sons or husbands, led their young daughters, kneeling down and kowtowing with each step, so they could rush to the mountain to burn incense. The mountainous road, covered with yellow dust and small and large pebbles for more than two days, was too much for the elderly and children to bear. On the way, they often fainted naturally, resting for a day at any village entrance or river crossing teahouse. Once their energy was restored, they continued walking, kneeling and kowtowing with each step. There were also those who made vows for their own illnesses or deaths. When they went to fulfill their vows, they bizarrely dressed as four-legged animals, crawling along with some pilgrims, draped in saddles and wearing bridles on their faces, just like a cart horse. However, a small incense burner was tied to the saddle, with incense burning inside. They crawled for hundreds of miles, the smoke from the burner always喷著non-stop. At night, they took down the incense burner, slept with the saddle on their backs, until they paid homage at the peak and climbed down the mountain.

Wealthy homeowners could donate robes, apply gold, and send plaques to the Holy Mother, and would not do such karmic things as making themselves into cattle and horses.

At the end of March, the pilgrims all walked towards home with walnuts, black dates, persimmon cakes, and some wild mountain fruits. By chance, there were spring rains those few days, and they were drenched like water chickens, but they still happily walked in the rain, telling each other:

"Someone fell down a slope at Dian Shan, this year the devil is scared."

"All that blood on the hillside!"

"At Yama's nose, a mother and daughter rolled into the mountain stream together."

They meant it was retribution for those who fell down the hillside and didn't repair it or respect the gods. I knew that on those narrow, treacherous mountain roads, where three people couldn't squeeze past each other, there was a chance of falling with a single misstep. Thousands of people crowded and poisoned each other as they crawled upwards, like ants. When someone fell from the hillside, people shouted wildly:

"Sinful, sinful!"

"The Holy Mother has eyes, retribution!"

No one cared, and by the time they rolled down with broken bones and shattered bones, the corpses no longer looked human. Many people gathered around to fabricate some absurd rumors to explain the sins of the deceased in their lifetime.

The residents of the mountain country were still ruled by gods. I thought of their simple character and hardworking spirit, and I also remembered how pitifully they were deceived.

They are like rocks, forgotten by modernity.

Nora (10) 200

— Illustration by Wan Chao Chen, Explanation by Xin Xin

While Mrs. Linton was asking who that person was, Dr. Nan Gai came out of Helmer's room.

Nora introduced them and read about the 'incurably morally ill' Krogstad, who had a position at the bank and was desperately calling for life.

Thinking of Krogstad being under Helmer's control, Nora happily stuffed macaroons into Nan Gai's mouth.

At this time, Helmer came out, and Nora introduced Mrs. Linton to him, along with a job.

When Helmer, Mrs. Linton, and Nan Gai went out together, they encountered Nora's 'little darlings' at the entrance.

Nora: Kitty, didn't you see? Aren't they lovely?

Helmer: Mrs. Linton, let's go. Only mothers can endure this cold.

Saving lives is the same as disaster relief

One more penny donated saves one more life

Temptation, Radio Drama Script by the Drama Troupe (25) 201

— Written by Liu Yawei

Sailor: The gangplank is being raised, no one is allowed to come down anymore! (Steamboat whistle sounds again)

Relief worker: Didn't I make it clear? No one famous is allowed on board! Are you deaf?

Sailor: (Shouts) The ship is leaving! (Sound of ship wheels churning water, iron striking, rudder turning)

Old Xiang: What's wrong? Little Lu hasn't finished his cake yet?

Little Lu: : No, I remembered how bitterly my brother died!

Fifth Aunt: (Sobbing) We don't even know where our father is!

Fifth Elder: (Comforting) Ah! Our lives are a free gift. I almost fell off the dam too!

Old Xiang: Why are you still talking about it? Who isn't sad! Who isn't upset! But... who can we blame?

(Dragging this group of heartbroken people stranded at the edge of the sea onto the waterway, the sound of the steamboat gradually fades away, leaving only the disturbed waves returning to the calm river surface. One can vaguely hear someone inside the ship saying: 'Who can we blame?').

Suzhou Ballad Singing 204

Cheng Fangzhou, Li Liansun, Mao Jiashu

Huamei (1060) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening 'Ode to the Red Cliff'

The romantic scholar was exiled to Huangzhou. He indulged in wandering by the river every day. On the fifteenth day of the seventh month of the Renxu year, he chatted with two or three close friends. Carefree, they boarded a boat at the Red Cliff. Soon, the moon rose from the east mountain, and they leaned on the railing, gazing at the stars. They struck the strings and sang to the bright moon. They frequently offered toasts to Li Bai. With clear song and subtle music, the guest echoed the sound. The guest was a Taoist priest from Western Sichuan, who played softly and harmonized melodiously. Like a lonely boat. How happy was Cao Mengde back then, composing poetry and wielding his spear with joy. He descended to Jiangling and conquered Jingzhou. Thousands of miles flowed smoothly with the wind. Indeed, he was a hero of his time, but where is he now? Thirty-six thousand days easily pass. How fortunate is human life, like a mayfly. One must see through vain fame and fortune. Speaking of poverty and success, I am ashamed. They washed their cups, drank, and gathered the food. The scattered cups and plates were not in order. They rested together on pillows in the small boat.

Cai Xiaofang's Record of Retribution

Sino-Western (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening 'Longing for Spring'

Green willows suddenly appear on the street. I lean alone on the railing, feeling depressed. Sorrow locks my brow, and my heart is drunk. I regret letting my husband go on a distant expedition. I only see the red and purple flowers in the clear garden, like brocade. Butterflies and bees complain and store up the good spring. The flourishing scenery fills me with resentment. I rely on caressing my jade zither to express my feelings. I only see that, burning incense, I press the icy strings. After playing a song, my heart is moved. My heart is anxious. My mind is deep. Counting the days, I eagerly await his return. At night, the lamp flower predicts good news, and in the morning, magpies are good omens. My troubled heart turns nine times and I am alarmed again. I don't know if he has a gentle乡 in another place. He doesn't care about my refinement and goes to marry elsewhere. If he lingers in the flowers and is unfaithful, I will treat the old and new with equal affection. I want to ask him, how will he comfort my娇嗔 when he returns? I have recently given up sewing. I am tired of leaning against the silver bed, suffering from illness. I hate that I can't abandon all kinds of longing. I resent that my dreams are upside down, and I am even more heartbroken. Fortunately, my neighboring sisters come to advise me. I should wear green embroidered shoes and go hiking. Remember that tomorrow is the Flower Festival. Beautiful flowers and金铃 . The birds sing on the branches with good news.
